The schema is given below:\\n47:  *\\n48:  * RecordBatch =>\\n49:  *  BaseOffset => Int64\\n50:  *  Length => Int32\\n51:  *  PartitionLeaderEpoch => Int32\\n52:  *  Magic => Int8\\n53:  *  CRC => Uint32\\n54:  *  Attributes => Int16\\n55:  *  LastOffsetDelta => Int32 // also serves as LastSequenceDelta\\n56:  *  BaseTimestamp => Int64\\n57:  *  MaxTimestamp => Int64\\n58:  *  ProducerId => Int64\\n59:  *  ProducerEpoch => Int16\\n60:  *  BaseSequence => Int32\\n61:  *  RecordsCount => Int32\\n62:  *  Records => [Record]\\n63:  *\\n64:  * Note that when compression is enabled (see attributes below), the compressed record data is serialized\\n65:  * directly following the count of the number of records.\\n66:  *\\n67:  * The CRC covers the data from the attributes to the end of the batch (i.e. all the bytes that follow the CRC). It is\\n68:  * located after the magic byte, which means that clients must parse the magic byte before deciding how to interpret\\n69:  * the bytes between the batch length and the magic byte. The partition leader epoch field is not included in the CRC\\n70:  * computation to avoid the need to recompute the CRC when this field is assigned for every batch that is received by\\n71:  * the broker. The CRC-32C (Castagnoli) polynomial is used for the computation.\\n72:  *\\n73:  * On Compaction: Unlike the older message formats, magic v2 and above preserves the first and last offset/sequence\\n74:  * numbers from the original batch when the log is cleaned. This is required in order to be able to restore the\\n75:  * producer's state when the log is reloaded. If we did not retain the last sequence number, then following\\n76:  * a partition leader failure, once the new leader has rebuilt the producer state from the log, the next sequence\\n77:  * expected number would no longer be in sync with what was written by the client. This would cause an\\n78:  * unexpected OutOfOrderSequence error, which is typically fatal. The base sequence number must be preserved for\\n79:  * duplicate checking: the broker checks incoming Produce requests for duplicates by verifying that the first and\\n80:  * last sequence numbers of the incoming batch match the last from that producer.\\n81:  *\\n82:  * Note that if all of the records in a batch are removed during compaction, the broker may still retain an empty\\n83:  * batch header in order to preserve the producer sequence information as described above. These empty batches\\n84:  * are retained only until either a new sequence number is written by the corresponding producer or the producerId\\n85:  * is expired from lack of activity.\\n86:  *\\n87:  * There is no similar need to preserve the timestamp from the original batch after compaction. The BaseTimestamp\\n88:  * field therefore reflects the timestamp of the first record in the batch in most cases. If the batch is empty, the\\n89:  * BaseTimestamp will be set to -1 (NO_TIMESTAMP). If the delete horizon flag is set to 1, the BaseTimestamp\\n90:  * will be set to the time at which tombstone records and aborted transaction markers in the batch should be removed.\\n91:  *\\n92:  * Similarly, the MaxTimestamp field reflects the maximum timestamp of the current records if the timestamp type\\n93:  * is CREATE_TIME. For LOG_APPEND_TIME, on the other hand, the MaxTimestamp field reflects the timestamp set\\n94:  * by the broker and is preserved after compaction. Additionally, the MaxTimestamp of an empty batch always retains\\n95:  * the previous value prior to becoming empty.\\n96:  *\\n97:  * The current attributes are given below:\\n98:  *\\n99:  *  ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\\n100:  *  | Unused (7-15) | Delete Horizon Flag (6) | Control (5) | Transactional (4) | Timestamp Type (3) | Compression Type (0-2) |\\n101:  *  ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\\n102:  */\\n103: public class DefaultRecordBatch extends The schema is given below:\\n47:  *\\n48:  * RecordBatch =>\\n49:  *  BaseOffset => Int64\\n50:  *  Length => Int32\\n51:  *  PartitionLeaderEpoch => Int32\\n52:  *  Magic => Int8\\n53:  *  CRC => Uint32\\n54:  *  Attributes => Int16\\n55:  *  LastOffsetDelta => Int32 // also serves as LastSequenceDelta\\n56:  *  BaseTimestamp => Int64\\n57:  *  MaxTimestamp => Int64\\n58:  *  ProducerId => Int64\\n59:  *  ProducerEpoch => Int16\\n60:  *  BaseSequence => Int32\\n61:  *  RecordsCount => Int32\\n62:  *  Records => [Record]\\n63:  *\\n64:  * Note that when compression is enabled (see attributes below), the compressed record data is serialized\\n65:  * directly following the count of the number of records.\\n66:  *\\n67:  * The CRC covers the data from the attributes to the end of the batch (i.e. all the bytes that follow the CRC). It is\\n68:  * located after the magic byte, which means that clients must parse the magic byte before deciding how to interpret\\n69:  * the bytes between the batch length and the magic byte. The partition leader epoch field is not included in the CRC\\n70:  * computation to avoid the need to recompute the CRC when this field is assigned for every batch that is received by\\n71:  * the broker. The CRC-32C (Castagnoli) polynomial is used for the computation.\\n72:  *\\n73:  * On Compaction: Unlike the older message formats, magic v2 and above preserves the first and last offset/sequence\\n74:  * numbers from the original batch when the log is cleaned. This is required in order to be able to restore the\\n75:  * producer's state when the log is reloaded. If we did not retain the last sequence number, then following\\n76:  * a partition leader failure, once the new leader has rebuilt the producer state from the log, the next sequence\\n77:  * expected number would no longer be in sync with what was written by the client. This would cause an\\n78:  * unexpected OutOfOrderSequence error, which is typically fatal. The base sequence number must be preserved for\\n79:  * duplicate checking: the broker checks incoming Produce requests for duplicates by verifying that the first and\\n80:  * last sequence numbers of the incoming batch match the last from that producer.\\n81:  *\\n82:  * Note that if all of the records in a batch are removed during compaction, the broker may still retain an empty\\n83:  * batch header in order to preserve the producer sequence information as described above. These empty batches\\n84:  * are retained only until either a new sequence number is written by the corresponding producer or the producerId\\n85:  * is expired from lack of activity.\\n86:  *\\n87:  * There is no similar need to preserve the timestamp from the original batch after compaction. The BaseTimestamp\\n88:  * field therefore reflects the timestamp of the first record in the batch in most cases. If the batch is empty, the\\n89:  * BaseTimestamp will be set to -1 (NO_TIMESTAMP). If the delete horizon flag is set to 1, the BaseTimestamp\\n90:  * will be set to the time at which tombstone records and aborted transaction markers in the batch should be removed.\\n91:  *\\n92:  * Similarly, the MaxTimestamp field reflects the maximum timestamp of the current records if the timestamp type\\n93:  * is CREATE_TIME. For LOG_APPEND_TIME, on the other hand, the MaxTimestamp field reflects the timestamp set\\n94:  * by the broker and is preserved after compaction. Additionally, the MaxTimestamp of an empty batch always retains\\n95:  * the previous value prior to becoming empty.\\n96:  *\\n97:  * The current attributes are given below:\\n98:  *\\n99:  *  ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\\n100:  *  | Unused (7-15) | Delete Horizon Flag (6) | Control (5) | Transactional (4) | Timestamp Type (3) | Compression Type (0-2) |\\n101:  *  ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\\n102:  */\\n103: public class DefaultRecordBatch extends /*\n2:  * Licensed to the Apache Software Foundation (ASF) under one or more\n3:  * contributor license agreements. The schema is given below:\n47:  *\n48:  * RecordBatch =>\n49:  *  BaseOffset => Int64\n50:  *  Length => Int32\n51:  *  PartitionLeaderEpoch => Int32\n52:  *  Magic => Int8\n53:  *  CRC => Uint32\n54:  *  Attributes => Int16\n55:  *  LastOffsetDelta => Int32 // also serves as LastSequenceDelta\n56:  *  BaseTimestamp => Int64\n57:  *  MaxTimestamp => Int64\n58:  *  ProducerId => Int64\n59:  *  ProducerEpoch => Int16\n60:  *  BaseSequence => Int32\n61:  *  RecordsCount => Int32\n62:  *  Records => [Record]\n63:  *\n64:  * Note that when compression is enabled (see attributes below), the compressed record data is serialized\n65:  * directly following the count of the number of records.\n66:  *\n67:  * The CRC covers the data from the attributes to the end of the batch (i.e. all the bytes that follow the CRC). It is\n68:  * located after the magic byte, which means that clients must parse the magic byte before deciding how to interpret\n69:  * the bytes between the batch length and the magic byte. The partition leader epoch field is not included in the CRC\n70:  * computation to avoid the need to recompute the CRC when this field is assigned for every batch that is received by\n71:  * the broker. The CRC-32C (Castagnoli) polynomial is used for the computation.\n72:  *\n73:  * On Compaction: Unlike the older message formats, magic v2 and above preserves the first and last offset/sequence\n74:  * numbers from the original batch when the log is cleaned. This is required in order to be able to restore the\n75:  * producer's state when the log is reloaded. If we did not retain the last sequence number, then following\n76:  * a partition leader failure, once the new leader has rebuilt the producer state from the log, the next sequence\n77:  * expected number would no longer be in sync with what was written by the client. This would cause an\n78:  * unexpected OutOfOrderSequence error, which is typically fatal. The base sequence number must be preserved for\n79:  * duplicate checking: the broker checks incoming Produce requests for duplicates by verifying that the first and\n80:  * last sequence numbers of the incoming batch match the last from that producer.\n81:  *\n82:  * Note that if all of the records in a batch are removed during compaction, the broker may still retain an empty\n83:  * batch header in order to preserve the producer sequence information as described above. These empty batches\n84:  * are retained only until either a new sequence number is written by the corresponding producer or the producerId\n85:  * is expired from lack of activity.\n86:  *\n87:  * There is no similar need to preserve the timestamp from the original batch after compaction. The BaseTimestamp\n88:  * field therefore reflects the timestamp of the first record in the batch in most cases. If the batch is empty, the\n89:  * BaseTimestamp will be set to -1 (NO_TIMESTAMP). If the delete horizon flag is set to 1, the BaseTimestamp\n90:  * will be set to the time at which tombstone records and aborted transaction markers in the batch should be removed.\n91:  *\n92:  * Similarly, the MaxTimestamp field reflects the maximum timestamp of the current records if the timestamp type\n93:  * is CREATE_TIME. For LOG_APPEND_TIME, on the other hand, the MaxTimestamp field reflects the timestamp set\n94:  * by the broker and is preserved after compaction. Additionally, the MaxTimestamp of an empty batch always retains\n95:  * the previous value prior to becoming empty.\n96:  *\n97:  * The current attributes are given below:\n98:  *\n99:  *  ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n100:  *  | Unused (7-15) | Delete Horizon Flag (6) | Control (5) | Transactional (4) | Timestamp Type (3) | Compression Type (0-2) |\n101:  *  ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n102:  */\n103: public class DefaultRecordBatch extends AbstractRecordBatch // Note that this differs from produce up-conversion where the timestamp type topic config is used and the log append\\n270:         // time is generated if the config is LOG_APPEND_TIME. The reason for the different behavior is that there is\\n271:         // no appropriate log append time we can generate at compaction time.\\n272:         TimestampType timestampType = originalBatch.timestampType() == TimestampType.NO_TIMESTAMP_TYPE ?\\n273:                 TimestampType.CREATE_TIME : originalBatch.timestampType();\\n274:         long logAppendTime = timestampType == TimestampType.LOG_APPEND_TIME ?\\n275:                 originalBatch.maxTimestamp() : RecordBatch.NO_TIMESTAMP;\\n276:         long baseOffset = originalBatch.magic() >= RecordBatch.MAGIC_VALUE_V2 ?\\n277:                 originalBatch.baseOffset() : retainedRecords.get(0).offset();\\n278: \\n279:         // Convert records with older record versions to the current one\\n280:         MemoryRecordsBuilder builder = new MemoryRecordsBuilder(bufferOutputStream, RecordBatch.CURRENT_MAGIC_VALUE,\\n281:                 compression, timestampType, baseOffset, logAppendTime, originalBatch.producerId(),\\n282:                 originalBatch.producerEpoch(), originalBatch.baseSequence(), originalBatch.isTransactional(),\\n283:                 originalBatch.isControlBatch(), originalBatch.partitionLeaderEpoch(), bufferOutputStream.limit(), deleteHorizonMs);\\n284: \\n285:         for (Record record : retainedRecords)\\n286:             builder.append(record);\\n287: \\n288:         if (originalBatch.magic() >= RecordBatch.MAGIC_VALUE_V2)\\n289:             // we must preserve the last offset from the initial batch in order to ensure that the\\n290:             // last sequence number from the batch remains even after compaction. Otherwise, the producer\\n291:             // could incorrectly see an out of sequence error.\\n292:             builder.overrideLastOffset(originalBatch.lastOffset());\\n293: \\n294:         return builder;\\n295:     }\\n296: \\n297:     /**\\n298:      * Get the byte buffer that backs this instance for reading.\\n299:      */\\n300:     public ByteBuffer buffer() {\\n301:         return buffer.duplicate();\\n302:     }\\n303: \\n304:     @Override\\n305:     public MemoryRecords slice(int position, int size) {\\n306:         if (position < 0)\\n307:             throw new IllegalArgumentException(\\\"Invalid position: \\\" + position + \\\" in read from \\\" + this);\\n308:         if (position > buffer.limit())\\n309:             throw new IllegalArgumentException(\\\"Slice from position \\\" + position + \\\" exceeds end position of \\\" + this);\\n310:         if (size < 0)\\n311:             throw new IllegalArgumentException(\\\"Invalid size: \\\" + size + \\\" in read from \\\" + this);\\n312: \\n313:         int availableBytes = Math.min(size, buffer.limit() - position);\\n314:         // As of now, clients module support Java11 hence can't use ByteBuffer::slice(position, size) method.\\n315:         // So we need to create a duplicate buffer and set the position and limit. Duplicate buffer\\n316:         // is backed by original bytes hence not the content but only the relative position and limit\\n317:         // are changed in the duplicate buffer. Once the position and limit are set, we can call the\\n318:         // slice method to get the sliced buffer, which is a backed by the original buffer with the\\n319:         // position reset to 0 and limit set to the size of the slice.\\n320:         ByteBuffer slicedBuffer = buffer.duplicate();\\n321:         slicedBuffer.position(position);\\n322:         slicedBuffer.limit(position + availableBytes);\\n323:         // Reset the position to 0 so that the sliced view has a relative position.\\n324:         slicedBuffer = slicedBuffer.slice();\\n325: \\n326:         return readableRecords(slicedBuffer);\\n327:     }\\n328: \\n329:     @Override\\n330:     public Iterable<MutableRecordBatch> batches() {\\n331:         return batches;\\n332:     }\\n333: \\n334:     @Override\\n335:     public String toString() {\\n336:         return \\\"MemoryRecords(size=\\\" + sizeInBytes() +\\n337:                 \\\", buffer=\\\" + buffer +\\n338:                 \\\")\\\";\\n339:     }\\n340: \\n341:     @Override\\n342:     public boolean equals(Object o) {\\n343:         if (this == o)\\n344:             return true;\\n345:         if (o == null || }\\n352: \\n353:     @Override\\n354:     public int hashCode() {\\n355:         return buffer.hashCode();\\n356:     }\\n357: \\n358:     public abstract static class RecordFilter {\\n359: MemoryRecordsBuilder buildRetainedRecordsInto(RecordBatch originalBatch,\n264:                                                                  List<Record> retainedRecords,\n265:                                                                  ByteBufferOutputStream bufferOutputStream,\n266:                                                                  final long deleteHorizonMs) {\n267: {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_014UZqe2ZmN6dByyyD7xSZei","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01NEDvGhXvgaoDiiPBUStZc6","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/RecordBatch.java","content":"/*\n * Licensed to the Apache Software Foundation (ASF) under one or more\n * contributor license agreements. See the NOTICE file distributed with\n * this work for additional information regarding copyright ownership.\n * The ASF licenses this file to You under the Apache License, Version 2.0\n * (the \"License\"); you may not use this file except in compliance with\n * the License. You may obtain a copy of the License at\n *\n *    http://www.apache.org/licenses/LICENSE-2.0\n *\n * Unless required by applicable law or agreed to in writing, software\n * distributed under the License is distributed on an \"AS IS\" BASIS,\n * WITHOUT WARRANTIES OR CONDITIONS OF ANY KIND, either express or implied.\n * See the License for the specific language governing permissions and\n * limitations under the License.\n */\npackage org.apache.kafka.common.record.internal;\n\nimport org.apache.kafka.common.record.TimestampType;\nimport org.apache.kafka.common.utils.BufferSupplier;\nimport org.apache.kafka.common.utils.CloseableIterator;\n\nimport java.nio.ByteBuffer;\nimport java.util.Iterator;\nimport java.util.Optional;\nimport java.util.OptionalLong;\n\n/**\n * A record batch is a container for records. In old versions of the record format (versions 0 and 1),\n * a batch consisted always of a single record if no compression was enabled, but could contain\n * many records otherwise. Newer versions (magic versions 2 and above) will generally contain many records\n * regardless of compression.\n *\n * <p><b>Thread Safety:</b> {@code RecordBatch} implementations are <b>not thread-safe</b>.\n * Callers must ensure external synchronization when accessing a batch from multiple threads.\n * However, multiple independent batches can be safely accessed concurrently.</p>\n *\n * <p><b>Protocol Role:</b> In the Kafka wire protocol, record batches are the fundamental unit of serialization.\n * Each batch contains a header with metadata (magic version, compression type, timestamps, offsets, producer ID, etc.)\n * followed by the actual record data. This interface provides read-only access to batch metadata and records,\n * allowing consumers and brokers to parse and iterate over log entries.</p>\n *\n * <p><b>Magic Versions:</b>\n * <ul>\n *   <li>Magic 0-1: Legacy format with limited metadata; single record if uncompressed</li>\n *   <li>Magic 2+: Current format with rich metadata; multiple records per batch</li>\n * </ul>\n * </p>\n */\npublic interface RecordBatch extends Iterable<Record> {\n\n    /**\n     * The \"magic\" values\n     */\n    byte MAGIC_VALUE_V0 = 0;\n    byte MAGIC_VALUE_V1 = 1;\n    byte MAGIC_VALUE_V2 = 2;\n\n    /**\n     * The current \"magic\" value\n     */\n    byte CURRENT_MAGIC_VALUE = MAGIC_VALUE_V2;\n\n    /**\n     * Timestamp value for records without a timestamp\n     */\n    long NO_TIMESTAMP = -1L;\n\n    /**\n     * Values used in the v2 record format by non-idempotent/non-transactional producers or when\n     * up-converting from an older format.\n     */\n    long NO_PRODUCER_ID = -1L;\n    short NO_PRODUCER_EPOCH = -1;\n    int NO_SEQUENCE = -1;\n\n    /**\n     * Used to indicate an unknown leader epoch, which will be the case when the record set is\n     * first created by the producer.\n     */\n    int NO_PARTITION_LEADER_EPOCH = -1;\n\n    /**\n     * Check whether the checksum of this batch is correct.\n     *\n     * @return {@code true} if the CRC-32C checksum is valid, {@code false} otherwise\n     */\n    boolean isValid();\n\n    /**\n     * Raise an exception if the checksum is not valid.\n     *\n     * @throws org.apache.kafka.common.errors.CorruptRecordException if the CRC does not match\n     */\n    void ensureValid();\n\n    /**\n     * Get the checksum of this record batch, which covers the batch header as well as all of the records.\n     * Uses CRC-32C (Castagnoli) polynomial for computation.\n     *\n     * @return The 4-byte unsigned checksum represented as a long\n     */\n    long checksum();\n\n    /**\n     * Get the max timestamp or log append time of this record batch.\n     *\n     * <p>If the timestamp type is {@link TimestampType#CREATE_TIME}, this is the maximum timestamp\n     * among all records contained in this batch. If the timestamp type is\n     * {@link TimestampType#LOG_APPEND_TIME}, this is the timestamp assigned by the broker.\n     * For magic version 0, this method returns {@link #NO_TIMESTAMP}.</p>\n     *\n     * @return The maximum timestamp in milliseconds since epoch, or {@link #NO_TIMESTAMP} if not set\n     */\n    long maxTimestamp();\n\n    /**\n     * Get the timestamp type of this record batch.\n     *\n     * <p>This indicates whether timestamps represent client creation time or broker log append time.\n     * Returns {@link TimestampType#NO_TIMESTAMP_TYPE} if the batch has magic 0.</p>\n     *\n     * @return The timestamp type, never null\n     * @see TimestampType\n     */\n    TimestampType timestampType();\n\n    /**\n     * Get the base offset contained in this record batch.\n     *\n     * <p>For magic version prior to 2, the base offset will always be the offset of the first message\n     * in the batch. This generally requires deep iteration over all records.\n     * For magic version 2 and above, this returns the first offset of the original record batch\n     * (i.e., prior to any log compaction). For non-compacted topics, the behavior is equivalent.</p>\n     *\n     * <p><b>Performance Note:</b> This method may require deep iteration for older magic versions,\n     * which can be expensive. Generally {@link #lastOffset()} is preferred since access is efficient\n     * for all magic versions.</p>\n     *\n     * @return The base offset of this record batch (which may or may not be the offset of the first\n     *         record, depending on log compaction)\n     */\n    long baseOffset();\n\n    /**\n     * Get the last offset in this record batch (inclusive).\n     *\n     * <p>This always reflects the offset of the last record in the original batch, even if records\n     * are removed during log compaction. This value is preserved across compaction operations.</p>\n     *\n     * @return The offset of the last record in this batch\n     */\n    long lastOffset();\n\n    /**\n     * Get the offset following this record batch (i.e. the last offset contained in this batch plus one).\n     *\n     * @return The next consecutive offset following this batch, equal to {@code lastOffset() + 1}\n     */\n    long nextOffset();\n\n    /**\n     * Get the record format version of this record batch (i.e. its magic value).\n     *\n     * <p>The magic value determines the binary format of the batch header and records within it.\n     * Common values are 0 (legacy), 1 (legacy), and 2 (current/recommended).</p>\n     *\n     * @return The magic byte indicating the record format version\n     */\n    byte magic();\n\n    /**\n     * Get the producer id for this log record batch.\n     *\n     * <p>The producer ID enables idempotent writes and transactional support. For older magic versions\n     * (0 and 1), or for non-idempotent producers, this returns {@link #NO_PRODUCER_ID}.</p>\n     *\n     * @return The producer ID, or {@link #NO_PRODUCER_ID} if not set or supported\n     */\n    long producerId();\n\n    /**\n     * Get the producer epoch for this log record batch.\n     *\n     * <p>The producer epoch works in conjunction with {@link #producerId()} to provide idempotent\n     * and transactional guarantees. The epoch increments when a producer attempts to recover from\n     * a failure.</p>\n     *\n     * @return The producer epoch, or {@link #NO_PRODUCER_EPOCH} if not set\n     */\n    short producerEpoch();\n\n    /**\n     * Check whether this batch has a valid producer id set.\n     *\n     * <p>This is equivalent to checking whether {@code producerId() != {@link #NO_PRODUCER_ID}}</p>\n     *\n     * @return {@code true} if this batch has an assigned producer ID, {@code false} otherwise\n     */\n    boolean hasProducerId();\n\n    /**\n     * Get the base sequence number of this record batch.\n     *\n     * <p>Like {@link #baseOffset()}, this value is not affected by compaction: it always retains\n     * the base sequence number from the original batch. Used for idempotent and transactional\n     * message deduplication.</p>\n     *\n     * @return The first sequence number, or {@link #NO_SEQUENCE} if none is set\n     */\n    int baseSequence();\n\n    /**\n     * Get the last sequence number of this record batch.\n     *\n     * <p>Like {@link #lastOffset()}, the last sequence number always reflects the sequence number\n     * of the last record in the original batch, even if records are removed during log compaction.</p>\n     *\n     * @return The last sequence number, or {@link #NO_SEQUENCE} if none is set\n     */\n    int lastSequence();\n\n    /**\n     * Get the compression type of this record batch.\n     *\n     * <p>This determines how the record data following the batch header is compressed.\n     * Compression is transparent to record iteration; callers receive decompressed records.</p>\n     *\n     * @return The {@link CompressionType}, never null\n     */\n    CompressionType compressionType();\n\n    /**\n     * Get the size in bytes of this batch, including the size of the record and the batch overhead.\n     *\n     * <p>This includes the batch header (approximately 56-61 bytes depending on magic version)\n     * plus all record data (compressed or uncompressed).</p>\n     *\n     * @return The size in bytes of this batch, always >= overhead for valid batches\n     */\n    int sizeInBytes();\n\n    /**\n     * Get the count of records in this batch if it is efficiently supported by the record format.\n     *\n     * <p><b>Performance Note:</b> For magic 2 and higher, the record count is stored in the batch header\n     * and is retrieved in O(1) time. For magic versions 0 and 1, deep iteration is required to count records,\n     * so this method returns {@code null} for backward compatibility.</p>\n     *\n     * @return The number of records in the batch, or {@code null} for magic versions 0 and 1 where\n     *         counting requires iteration\n     */\n    Integer countOrNull();\n\n    /**\n     * Check whether this record batch is compressed.\n     *\n     * <p>If true, the record data (after the batch header) is compressed according to\n     * {@link #compressionType()}. Decompression happens transparently during iteration.</p>\n     *\n     * @return {@code true} if compression is enabled, {@code false} otherwise\n     */\n    boolean isCompressed();\n\n    /**\n     * Write this record batch into a buffer.\n     *\n     * <p><b>Performance Note:</b> This is a zero-copy operation that duplicates the backing buffer.\n     * No decompression occurs; the batch is written in its serialized form.</p>\n     *\n     * @param buffer The {@link ByteBuffer} to write the batch to; must have at least\n     *               {@link #sizeInBytes()} remaining bytes\n     */\n    void writeTo(ByteBuffer buffer);\n\n    /**\n     * Whether or not this record batch is part of a transaction.\n     *\n     * <p>Transactional batches are marked with a flag in the batch attributes and are used to\n     * implement exactly-once semantics and atomic multi-partition writes.</p>\n     *\n     * @return {@code true} if this batch is transactional, {@code false} otherwise\n     */\n    boolean isTransactional();\n\n    /**\n     * Get the delete horizon, which indicates the timestamp at which records with earlier timestamps\n     * (tomb stones and aborted transaction markers) in this batch should be removed.\n     *\n     * <p>The delete horizon is used during log compaction to ensure correct behavior with tombstones\n     * and aborted transactional markers. Returns empty if no delete horizon is set.</p>\n     *\n     * @return An {@link OptionalLong} containing the delete horizon timestamp in milliseconds,\n     *         or empty if not set\n     */\n    OptionalLong deleteHorizonMs();\n\n    /**\n     * Get the partition leader epoch of this record batch.\n     *\n     * <p>The leader epoch is used by the broker to detect leadership changes and is not included\n     * in the CRC computation to allow brokers to update it in-place for each received batch.</p>\n     *\n     * @return The leader epoch, or {@link #NO_PARTITION_LEADER_EPOCH} if unknown\n     */\n    int partitionLeaderEpoch();\n\n    /**\n     * Return a streaming iterator which delays decompression of the record stream until records\n     * are actually requested using {@link Iterator#next()}.\n     *\n     * <p><b>Performance Note:</b> For compressed batches, this enables memory-efficient iteration\n     * by decompressing data on-demand rather than loading the entire decompressed stream into memory.\n     * The buffer supplier parameter allows callers to reuse decompression buffers, which is\n     * critical for performance. For small batches (< 64KB), allocating a large buffer (e.g., 64 KB for LZ4)\n     * can dominate the cost of decompression.</p>\n     *\n     * <p><b>Resource Management:</b> The returned iterator must be closed to release decompression\n     * resources. Consider using try-with-resources.</p>\n     *\n     * @param decompressionBufferSupplier The supplier of {@link ByteBuffer}s used for decompression\n     *                                    if the batch is compressed. Suppliers that reuse buffers across\n     *                                    iterations have significant performance impact.\n     * @return A {@link CloseableIterator} over {@link Record}s in this batch; must be closed by caller\n     */\n    CloseableIterator<Record> streamingIterator(BufferSupplier decompressionBufferSupplier);\n\n    /**\n     * Check whether this is a control batch (i.e., whether the control bit is set in the batch attributes).\n     *\n     * <p>Control batches contain special messages used for transactional markers and coordination,\n     * not application data records. For magic versions prior to 2, this is always false.</p>\n     *\n     * @return {@code true} if this batch contains control records, {@code false} if it contains data records\n     */\n    boolean isControlBatch();\n\n    /**\n     * Iterate all records to find the offset of the record with maximum timestamp.\n     *\n     * <p><b>Behavior Notes:</b>\n     * <ul>\n     *   <li>If multiple records share the maximum timestamp, returns the offset of the earliest one</li>\n     *   <li>For magic version 0, always returns empty since timestamps are not supported</li>\n     *   <li>This requires full iteration over all records in the batch, which may be expensive</li>\n     * </ul>\n     * </p>\n     *\n     * @return An {@link Optional} containing the offset of the record with maximum timestamp,\n     *         or empty if no records exist or magic version is 0\n     * @see #maxTimestamp()\n     * @see #streamingIterator(BufferSupplier)\n     */\n    default Optional<Long> offsetOfMaxTimestamp() {\n        if (magic() == RecordBatch.MAGIC_VALUE_V0) return Optional.empty();\n        long maxTimestamp = maxTimestamp();\n        try (CloseableIterator<Record> iter = streamingIterator(BufferSupplier.create())) {\n            while (iter.hasNext()) {\n                Record record = iter.next();\n                if (maxTimestamp == record.timestamp()) return Optional.of(record.offset());\n            }\n        }\n        return Optional.empty();\n    }\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":10,"cache_creation_input_tokens":602,"cache_read_input_tokens":67236,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":602},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"460062e3-2618-4cae-a634-e96d3c95325f","uuid":"0b8eae38-0bfa-4aeb-b4a5-64e1bd2b4d79"}

In old versions of the record format (versions 0 and 1),\n * a batch consisted always of a single record if no compression was enabled, but could contain\n * many records otherwise. Newer versions (magic versions 2 and above) will generally contain many records\n * regardless of compression.\n *\n * <p><b>Thread Safety:</b> {@code RecordBatch} implementations are <b>not thread-safe</b>.\n * Callers must ensure external synchronization when accessing a batch from multiple threads.\n * However, multiple independent batches can be safely accessed concurrently.</p>\n *\n * <p><b>Protocol Role:</b> In the Kafka wire protocol, record batches are the fundamental unit of serialization.\n * Each batch contains a header with metadata (magic version, compression type, timestamps, offsets, producer ID, etc.)\n * followed by the actual record data. This interface provides read-only access to batch metadata and records,\n * allowing consumers and brokers to parse and iterate over log entries.</p>\n *\n * <p><b>Magic Versions:</b>\n * <ul>\n *   <li>Magic 0-1: Legacy format with limited metadata; single record if uncompressed</li>\n *   <li>Magic 2+: Current format with rich metadata; multiple records per batch</li>\n * </ul>\n * </p>\n */\npublic interface RecordBatch extends Iterable<Record> {\n\n    /**\n     * The \"magic\" values\n     */\n    byte MAGIC_VALUE_V0 = 0;\n    byte MAGIC_VALUE_V1 = 1;\n    byte MAGIC_VALUE_V2 = 2;\n\n    /**\n     * The current \"magic\" value\n     */\n    byte CURRENT_MAGIC_VALUE = MAGIC_VALUE_V2;\n\n    /**\n     * Timestamp value for records without a timestamp\n     */\n    long NO_TIMESTAMP = -1L;\n\n    /**\n     * Values used in the v2 record format by non-idempotent/non-transactional producers or when\n     * up-converting from an older format.\n     */\n    long NO_PRODUCER_ID = -1L;\n    short NO_PRODUCER_EPOCH = -1;\n    int NO_SEQUENCE = -1;\n\n    /**\n     * Used to indicate an unknown leader epoch, which will be the case when the record set is\n     * first created by the producer.\n     */\n    int NO_PARTITION_LEADER_EPOCH = -1;\n\n    /**\n     * Check whether the checksum of this batch is correct.\n     *\n     * @return {@code true} if the CRC-32C checksum is valid, {@code false} otherwise\n     */\n    boolean isValid();\n\n    /**\n     * Raise an exception if the checksum is not valid.\n     *\n     * @throws org.apache.kafka.common.errors.CorruptRecordException if the CRC does not match\n     */\n    void ensureValid();\n\n    /**\n     * Get the checksum of this record batch, which covers the batch header as well as all of the records.\n     * Uses CRC-32C (Castagnoli) polynomial for computation.\n     *\n     * @return The 4-byte unsigned checksum represented as a long\n     */\n    long checksum();\n\n    /**\n     * Get the max timestamp or log append time of this record batch.\n     *\n     * <p>If the timestamp type is {@link TimestampType#CREATE_TIME}, this is the maximum timestamp\n     * among all records contained in this batch. If the timestamp type is\n     * {@link TimestampType#LOG_APPEND_TIME}, this is the timestamp assigned by the broker.\n     * For magic version 0, this method returns {@link #NO_TIMESTAMP}.</p>\n     *\n     * @return The maximum timestamp in milliseconds since epoch, or {@link #NO_TIMESTAMP} if not set\n     */\n    long maxTimestamp();\n\n    /**\n     * Get the timestamp type of this record batch.\n     *\n     * <p>This indicates whether timestamps represent client creation time or broker log append time.\n     * Returns {@link TimestampType#NO_TIMESTAMP_TYPE} if the batch has magic 0.</p>\n     *\n     * @return The timestamp type, never null\n     * @see TimestampType\n     */\n    TimestampType timestampType();\n\n    /**\n     * Get the base offset contained in this record batch.\n     *\n     * <p>For magic version prior to 2, the base offset will always be the offset of the first message\n     * in the batch. This generally requires deep iteration over all records.\n     * For magic version 2 and above, this returns the first offset of the original record batch\n     * (i.e., prior to any log compaction). For non-compacted topics, the behavior is equivalent.</p>\n     *\n     * <p><b>Performance Note:</b> This method may require deep iteration for older magic versions,\n     * which can be expensive. Generally {@link #lastOffset()} is preferred since access is efficient\n     * for all magic versions.</p>\n     *\n     * @return The base offset of this record batch (which may or may not be the offset of the first\n     *         record, depending on log compaction)\n     */\n    long baseOffset();\n\n    /**\n     * Get the last offset in this record batch (inclusive).\n     *\n     * <p>This always reflects the offset of the last record in the original batch, even if records\n     * are removed during log compaction. This value is preserved across compaction operations.</p>\n     *\n     * @return The offset of the last record in this batch\n     */\n    long lastOffset();\n\n    /**\n     * Get the offset following this record batch (i.e. the last offset contained in this batch plus one).\n     *\n     * @return The next consecutive offset following this batch, equal to {@code lastOffset() + 1}\n     */\n    long nextOffset();\n\n    /**\n     * Get the record format version of this record batch (i.e. its magic value).\n     *\n     * <p>The magic value determines the binary format of the batch header and records within it.\n     * Common values are 0 (legacy), 1 (legacy), and 2 (current/recommended).</p>\n     *\n     * @return The magic byte indicating the record format version\n     */\n    byte magic();\n\n    /**\n     * Get the producer id for this log record batch.\n     *\n     * <p>The producer ID enables idempotent writes and transactional support. For older magic versions\n     * (0 and 1), or for non-idempotent producers, this returns {@link #NO_PRODUCER_ID}.</p>\n     *\n     * @return The producer ID, or {@link #NO_PRODUCER_ID} if not set or supported\n     */\n    long producerId();\n\n    /**\n     * Get the producer epoch for this log record batch.\n     *\n     * <p>The producer epoch works in conjunction with {@link #producerId()} to provide idempotent\n     * and transactional guarantees. The epoch increments when a producer attempts to recover from\n     * a failure.</p>\n     *\n     * @return The producer epoch, or {@link #NO_PRODUCER_EPOCH} if not set\n     */\n    short producerEpoch();\n\n    /**\n     * Check whether this batch has a valid producer id set.\n     *\n     * <p>This is equivalent to checking whether {@code producerId() != {@link #NO_PRODUCER_ID}}</p>\n     *\n     * @return {@code true} if this batch has an assigned producer ID, {@code false} otherwise\n     */\n    boolean hasProducerId();\n\n    /**\n     * Get the base sequence number of this record batch.\n     *\n     * <p>Like {@link #baseOffset()}, this value is not affected by compaction: it always retains\n     * the base sequence number from the original batch. Used for idempotent and transactional\n     * message deduplication.</p>\n     *\n     * @return The first sequence number, or {@link #NO_SEQUENCE} if none is set\n     */\n    int baseSequence();\n\n    /**\n     * Get the last sequence number of this record batch.\n     *\n     * <p>Like {@link #lastOffset()}, the last sequence number always reflects the sequence number\n     * of the last record in the original batch, even if records are removed during log compaction.</p>\n     *\n     * @return The last sequence number, or {@link #NO_SEQUENCE} if none is set\n     */\n    int lastSequence();\n\n    /**\n     * Get the compression type of this record batch.\n     *\n     * <p>This determines how the record data following the batch header is compressed.\n     * Compression is transparent to record iteration; callers receive decompressed records.</p>\n     *\n     * @return The {@link CompressionType}, never null\n     */\n    CompressionType compressionType();\n\n    /**\n     * Get the size in bytes of this batch, including the size of the record and the batch overhead.\n     *\n     * <p>This includes the batch header (approximately 56-61 bytes depending on magic version)\n     * plus all record data (compressed or uncompressed).</p>\n     *\n     * @return The size in bytes of this batch, always >= overhead for valid batches\n     */\n    int sizeInBytes();\n\n    /**\n     * Get the count of records in this batch if it is efficiently supported by the record format.\n     *\n     * <p><b>Performance Note:</b> For magic 2 and higher, the record count is stored in the batch header\n     * and is retrieved in O(1) time. For magic versions 0 and 1, deep iteration is required to count records,\n     * so this method returns {@code null} for backward compatibility.</p>\n     *\n     * @return The number of records in the batch, or {@code null} for magic versions 0 and 1 where\n     *         counting requires iteration\n     */\n    Integer countOrNull();\n\n    /**\n     * Check whether this record batch is compressed.\n     *\n     * <p>If true, the record data (after the batch header) is compressed according to\n     * {@link #compressionType()}. Decompression happens transparently during iteration.</p>\n     *\n     * @return {@code true} if compression is enabled, {@code false} otherwise\n     */\n    boolean isCompressed();\n\n    /**\n     * Write this record batch into a buffer.\n     *\n     * <p><b>Performance Note:</b> This is a zero-copy operation that duplicates the backing buffer.\n     * No decompression occurs; the batch is written in its serialized form.</p>\n     *\n     * @param buffer The {@link ByteBuffer} to write the batch to; must have at least\n     *               {@link #sizeInBytes()} remaining bytes\n     */\n    void writeTo(ByteBuffer buffer);\n\n    /**\n     * Whether or not this record batch is part of a transaction.\n     *\n     * <p>Transactional batches are marked with a flag in the batch attributes and are used to\n     * implement exactly-once semantics and atomic multi-partition writes.</p>\n     *\n     * @return {@code true} if this batch is transactional, {@code false} otherwise\n     */\n    boolean isTransactional();\n\n    /**\n     * Get the delete horizon, which indicates the timestamp at which records with earlier timestamps\n     * (tomb stones and aborted transaction markers) in this batch should be removed.\n     *\n     * <p>The delete horizon is used during log compaction to ensure correct behavior with tombstones\n     * and aborted transactional markers. Returns empty if no delete horizon is set.</p>\n     *\n     * @return An {@link OptionalLong} containing the delete horizon timestamp in milliseconds,\n     *         or empty if not set\n     */\n    OptionalLong deleteHorizonMs();\n\n    /**\n     * Get the partition leader epoch of this record batch.\n     *\n     * <p>The leader epoch is used by the broker to detect leadership changes and is not included\n     * in the CRC computation to allow brokers to update it in-place for each received batch.</p>\n     *\n     * @return The leader epoch, or {@link #NO_PARTITION_LEADER_EPOCH} if unknown\n     */\n    int partitionLeaderEpoch();\n\n    /**\n     * Return a streaming iterator which delays decompression of the record stream until records\n     * are actually requested using {@link Iterator#next()}.\n     *\n     * <p><b>Performance Note:</b> For compressed batches, this enables memory-efficient iteration\n     * by decompressing data on-demand rather than loading the entire decompressed stream into memory.\n     * The buffer supplier parameter allows callers to reuse decompression buffers, which is\n     * critical for performance. For small batches (< 64KB), allocating a large buffer (e.g., 64 KB for LZ4)\n     * can dominate the cost of decompression.</p>\n     *\n     * <p><b>Resource Management:</b> The returned iterator must be closed to release decompression\n     * resources. Consider using try-with-resources.</p>\n     *\n     * @param decompressionBufferSupplier The supplier of {@link ByteBuffer}s used for decompression\n     *                                    if the batch is compressed. Suppliers that reuse buffers across\n     *                                    iterations have significant performance impact.\n     * @return A {@link CloseableIterator} over {@link Record}s in this batch; must be closed by caller\n     */\n    CloseableIterator<Record> streamingIterator(BufferSupplier decompressionBufferSupplier);\n\n    /**\n     * Check whether this is a control batch (i.e., whether the control bit is set in the batch attributes).\n     *\n     * <p>Control batches contain special messages used for transactional markers and coordination,\n     * not application data records. For magic versions prior to 2, this is always false.</p>\n     *\n     * @return {@code true} if this batch contains control records, {@code false} if it contains data records\n     */\n    boolean isControlBatch();\n\n    /**\n     * Iterate all records to find the offset of the record with maximum timestamp.\n     *\n     * <p><b>Behavior Notes:</b>\n     * <ul>\n     *   <li>If multiple records share the maximum timestamp, returns the offset of the earliest one</li>\n     *   <li>For magic version 0, always returns empty since timestamps are not supported</li>\n     *   <li>This requires full iteration over all records in the batch, which may be expensive</li>\n     * </ul>\n     * </p>\n     *\n     * @return An {@link Optional} containing the offset of the record with maximum timestamp,\n     *         or empty if no records exist or magic version is 0\n     * @see #maxTimestamp()\n     * @see #streamingIterator(BufferSupplier)\n     */\n    default Optional<Long> offsetOfMaxTimestamp() {\n        if (magic() == RecordBatch.MAGIC_VALUE_V0) return Optional.empty();\n        long maxTimestamp = maxTimestamp();\n        try (CloseableIterator<Record> iter = streamingIterator(BufferSupplier.create())) {\n            while (iter.hasNext()) {\n                Record record = iter.next();\n                if (maxTimestamp == record.timestamp()) return Optional.of(record.offset());\n            }\n        }\n        return Optional.empty();\n    }\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
