This is typically used for:\n * <ul>\n *   <li>Reading incoming produce requests from clients</li>\n *   <li>Reading log segments from disk (after loading into memory)</li>\n *   <li>Filtering records during log compaction</li>\n *   <li>Validating record batches for correctness</li>\n * </ul>\n * </p>\n *\n * <p><b>Construction:</b> To create a new buffer of record batches, use {@link #builder(ByteBuffer, byte, Compression, TimestampType, long)}\n * or one of its variants. For reading existing data, use {@link #readableRecords(ByteBuffer)}.</p>\n *\n * <p><b>Thread Safety:</b> {@code MemoryRecords} instances are <b>not thread-safe</b> for concurrent\n * modification, but the underlying buffer is typically immutable after construction. Multiple threads\n * may safely read from the same instance concurrently if the buffer contents are not being modified.</p>\n *\n * <p><b>Memory Efficiency:</b> The buffer is stored as-is without copying. The {@link #buffer()} method\n * returns a duplicate to prevent unintended position changes from affecting batch iteration.</p>\n *\n * <p><b>Lazy Evaluation:</b> Batch iteration is lazy; batches are parsed on-demand as you iterate.\n * Validation (via {@link RecordBatch#isValid()}) is not automatic and must be explicitly requested.</p>\n *\n * @see RecordBatch\n * @see MemoryRecordsBuilder\n * @see Records\n */\npublic class MemoryRecords extends AbstractRecords {\n    /**\n     * An empty {@code MemoryRecords} instance, useful as a sentinel or default value.\n     */\n    public static final MemoryRecords EMPTY = MemoryRecords.readableRecords(ByteBuffer.allocate(0));\n\n    private final ByteBuffer buffer;\n\n    private final Iterable<MutableRecordBatch> batches = this::batchIterator;\n\n    private int validBytes = -1;\n\n    /**\n     * Construct a {@code MemoryRecords} backed by the given buffer.\n     *\n     * <p><b>Ownership:</b> The caller retains ownership of the buffer. The buffer must remain\n     * valid and unmodified during the lifetime of this instance.</p>\n     *\n     * @param buffer A {@link ByteBuffer} containing one or more serialized record batches.\n     *               Must not be null.\n     * @throws NullPointerException if buffer is null\n     */\n    private MemoryRecords(ByteBuffer buffer) {\n        Objects.requireNonNull(buffer, \"buffer should not be null\");\n        this.buffer = buffer;\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public int sizeInBytes() {\n        return buffer.limit();\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Write a portion of these records to the given channel.\n     *\n     * <p><b>Partial Writes:</b> This method supports writing a subset of the records buffer.\n     * The {@code position} and {@code length} parameters define the slice to be written.</p>\n     *\n     * @param channel The {@link TransferableChannel} to write to\n     * @param position The starting position within this buffer (0-based)\n     * @param length The number of bytes to write\n     * @return The number of bytes actually written\n     * @throws IOException If an I/O error occurs\n     * @throws IllegalArgumentException If position + length exceeds buffer limit\n     */\n    @Override\n    public int writeTo(TransferableChannel channel, int position, int length) throws IOException {\n        if (((long) position) + length > buffer.limit())\n            throw new IllegalArgumentException(\"position+length should not be greater than buffer.limit(), position: \"\n                    + position + \", length: \" + length + \", buffer.limit(): \" + buffer.limit());\n\n        return Utils.tryWriteTo(channel, position, length, buffer);\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Write all records to the given channel, including any partial trailing records.\n     *\n     * <p><b>Completeness:</b> Unlike {@link #writeTo(TransferableChannel, int, int)},\n     * this method writes the entire buffer including potentially incomplete batches at the end.</p>\n     *\n     * @param channel The {@link GatheringByteChannel} to write to\n     * @return The total number of bytes written\n     * @throws IOException For any I/O errors writing to the channel\n     */\n    public int writeFullyTo(GatheringByteChannel channel) throws IOException {\n        buffer.mark();\n        int written = 0;\n        while (written < sizeInBytes())\n            written += channel.write(buffer);\n        buffer.reset();\n        return written;\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Get the total number of bytes in this record set representing valid, complete record batches.\n     *\n     * <p><b>Valid vs. Complete:</b> This returns the sum of sizes of all successfully parsed batches.\n     * If the buffer ends with a partial or corrupt batch, that partial data is not included.\n     * This may be smaller than {@link #sizeInBytes()}.</p>\n     *\n     * <p><b>Caching:</b> This value is computed once and then cached on first access.\n     * If batches are modified in-place, the cache becomes stale.</p>\n     *\n     * @return The number of valid bytes, excluding any trailing partial batches\n     */\n    public int validBytes() {\n        if (validBytes >= 0)\n            return validBytes;\n\n        int bytes = 0;\n        for (RecordBatch batch : batches())\n            bytes += batch.sizeInBytes();\n\n        this.validBytes = bytes;\n        return bytes;\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public AbstractIterator<MutableRecordBatch> batchIterator() {\n        return new RecordBatchIterator<>(new ByteBufferLogInputStream(buffer.duplicate(), Integer.MAX_VALUE));\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Validate the header of the first batch and return its size.\n     *\n     * <p><b>Partial Validation:</b> This method validates only the batch header structure,\n     * not the record data or CRC. It is useful for determining if enough data has been received.</p>\n     *\n     * @return The first batch size including {@link Records#LOG_OVERHEAD} if the buffer contains\n     *         a complete header up to the magic byte, or null if insufficient data\n     * @throws CorruptRecordException If the record size is invalid or the magic byte is unrecognized\n     */\n    public Integer firstBatchSize() {\n        if (buffer.remaining() < HEADER_SIZE_UP_TO_MAGIC)\n            return null;\n        return new ByteBufferLogInputStream(buffer, Integer.MAX_VALUE).nextBatchSize();\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Filter the records in this batch according to the provided filter function.\n     *\n     * <p><b>Filtering Strategy:</b> For each batch, the filter is consulted to determine if the\n     * entire batch should be deleted, whether to retain empty batches, or whether to inspect\n     * individual records. Records may be selectively retained or discarded based on the filter.</p>\n     *\n     * <p><b>Output Buffer Management:</b> If the filtered output does not fit in the provided\n     * {@code destinationBuffer}, a new buffer is allocated and returned in the {@link FilterResult}.</p>\n     *\n     * <p><b>Compaction Support:</b> If filtered records contain tombstones or aborted transaction markers,\n     * the delete horizon is automatically set to enable proper tombstone cleanup during future compaction.</p>\n     *\n     * <p><b>Performance Tuning:</b> The {@code decompressionBufferSupplier} is critical for performance.\n     * A supplier that reuses buffers across calls significantly improves throughput, especially for\n     * LZ4 compression which requires 64 KB buffers.</p>\n     *\n     * @param filter The {@link RecordFilter} that determines retention policy\n     * @param destinationBuffer The {@link ByteBuffer} to write filtered records to;\n     *                          may be replaced in the result if insufficient capacity\n     * @param decompressionBufferSupplier A supplier for decompression buffers. Reusing buffers\n     *                                    across calls is critical for performance.\n     * @return A {@link FilterResult} containing the output buffer, retained record counts,\n     *         and metadata for metrics\n     * @see RecordFilter\n     * @see FilterResult\n     */\n    public FilterResult filterTo(RecordFilter filter, ByteBuffer destinationBuffer, BufferSupplier decompressionBufferSupplier) {\n        return filterTo(batches(), filter, destinationBuffer, decompressionBufferSupplier);\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Note: This method is also used to convert the first timestamp of the batch (which is usually the timestamp of the first record)\n     * to the delete horizon of the tombstones or txn markers which are present in the batch.\n     */\n    private static FilterResult filterTo(Iterable<MutableRecordBatch> batches, RecordFilter filter,\n                                         ByteBuffer destinationBuffer, BufferSupplier decompressionBufferSupplier) {\n        FilterResult filterResult = new FilterResult(destinationBuffer);\n        ByteBufferOutputStream bufferOutputStream = new ByteBufferOutputStream(destinationBuffer);\n        for (MutableRecordBatch batch : batches) {\n            final BatchRetentionResult batchRetentionResult = filter.checkBatchRetention(batch);\n            final boolean containsMarkerForEmptyTxn = batchRetentionResult.containsMarkerForEmptyTxn;\n            final BatchRetention batchRetention = batchRetentionResult.batchRetention;\n\n            filterResult.bytesRead += batch.sizeInBytes();\n\n            if (batchRetention == BatchRetention.DELETE)\n                continue;\n\n            final BatchFilterResult iterationResult = filterBatch(batch, decompressionBufferSupplier, filterResult,\n                filter);\n            List<Record> retainedRecords = iterationResult.retainedRecords;\n            boolean containsTombstones = iterationResult.containsTombstones;\n            boolean writeOriginalBatch = iterationResult.writeOriginalBatch;\n            long maxOffset = iterationResult.maxOffset;\n\n            if (!retainedRecords.isEmpty()) {\n                // we check if the delete horizon should be set to a new value\n                // in which case, we need to reset the base timestamp and overwrite the timestamp deltas\n                // if the batch does not contain tombstones, then we don't need to overwrite batch\n                boolean needToSetDeleteHorizon = (containsTombstones || containsMarkerForEmptyTxn) &&\n                    batch.deleteHorizonMs().isEmpty();\n                if (writeOriginalBatch && !needToSetDeleteHorizon) {\n                    batch.writeTo(bufferOutputStream);\n                    filterResult.updateRetainedBatchMetadata(batch, retainedRecords.size(), false);\n                } else {\n                    long deleteHorizonMs;\n                    if (needToSetDeleteHorizon)\n                        deleteHorizonMs = filter.currentTime + filter.deleteRetentionMs;\n                    else\n                        deleteHorizonMs = batch.deleteHorizonMs().orElse(RecordBatch.NO_TIMESTAMP);\n                    try (final MemoryRecordsBuilder builder = buildRetainedRecordsInto(batch, retainedRecords,\n                            bufferOutputStream, deleteHorizonMs)) {\n                        MemoryRecords records = builder.build();\n                        int filteredBatchSize = records.sizeInBytes();\n                        MemoryRecordsBuilder.RecordsInfo info = builder.info();\n                        filterResult.updateRetainedBatchMetadata(info.maxTimestamp, info.shallowOffsetOfMaxTimestamp,\n                            maxOffset, retainedRecords.size(), filteredBatchSize);\n                    }\n                }\n            } else if (batchRetention == BatchRetention.RETAIN_EMPTY) {\n                if (batch.magic() < RecordBatch.MAGIC_VALUE_V2) // should never happen\n                    throw new IllegalStateException(\"Empty batches are only supported for magic v2 and above\");\n\n                bufferOutputStream.ensureRemaining(DefaultRecordBatch.RECORD_BATCH_OVERHEAD);\n                DefaultRecordBatch.writeEmptyHeader(bufferOutputStream.buffer(), RecordBatch.CURRENT_MAGIC_VALUE, batch.producerId(),\n                        batch.producerEpoch(), batch.baseSequence(), batch.baseOffset(), batch.lastOffset(),\n                        batch.partitionLeaderEpoch(), batch.timestampType(), batch.maxTimestamp(),\n                        batch.isTransactional(), batch.isControlBatch());\n                filterResult.updateRetainedBatchMetadata(batch, 0, true);\n            }\n\n            // If we had to allocate a new buffer to fit the filtered buffer (see KAFKA-5316), return early to\n            // avoid the need for additional allocations.\n            ByteBuffer outputBuffer = bufferOutputStream.buffer();\n            if (outputBuffer != destinationBuffer) {\n                filterResult.outputBuffer = outputBuffer;\n                return filterResult;\n            }\n        }\n\n        return filterResult;\n    }\n\n    private static BatchFilterResult filterBatch(RecordBatch batch,\n                                                 BufferSupplier decompressionBufferSupplier,\n                                                 FilterResult filterResult,\n                                                 RecordFilter filter) {\n        try (final CloseableIterator<Record> iterator = batch.streamingIterator(decompressionBufferSupplier)) {\n            long maxOffset = -1;\n            boolean containsTombstones = false;\n            // Convert records with old record versions\n            boolean writeOriginalBatch = batch.magic() >= RecordBatch.CURRENT_MAGIC_VALUE;\n            List<Record> retainedRecords = new ArrayList<>();\n            while (iterator.hasNext()) {\n                Record record = iterator.next();\n                filterResult.messagesRead += 1;\n\n                if (filter.shouldRetainRecord(batch, record)) {\n                    if (record.offset() > maxOffset)\n                        maxOffset = record.offset();\n\n                    retainedRecords.add(record);\n\n                    if (!record.hasValue()) {\n                        containsTombstones = true;\n                    }\n                } else {\n                    writeOriginalBatch = false;\n                }\n            }\n            return new BatchFilterResult(retainedRecords, writeOriginalBatch, containsTombstones, maxOffset);\n        }\n    }\n\n    private static class BatchFilterResult {\n        private final List<Record> retainedRecords;\n        private final boolean writeOriginalBatch;\n        private final boolean containsTombstones;\n        private final long maxOffset;\n        private BatchFilterResult(List<Record> retainedRecords,\n                                  final boolean writeOriginalBatch,\n                                  final boolean containsTombstones,\n                                  final long maxOffset) {\n            this.retainedRecords = retainedRecords;\n            this.writeOriginalBatch = writeOriginalBatch;\n            this.containsTombstones = containsTombstones;\n            this.maxOffset = maxOffset;\n        }\n    }\n\n    private static MemoryRecordsBuilder buildRetainedRecordsInto(RecordBatch originalBatch,\n                                                                 List<Record> retainedRecords,\n                                                                 ByteBufferOutputStream bufferOutputStream,\n                                                                 final long deleteHorizonMs) {\n        Compression compression = Compression.of(originalBatch.compressionType()).build();\n        // V0 has no timestamp type or timestamp, so we set the timestamp to CREATE_TIME and timestamp to NO_TIMESTAMP.\n        // Note that this differs from produce up-conversion where the timestamp type topic config is used and the log append\n        // time is generated if the config is LOG_APPEND_TIME. The reason for the different behavior is that there is\n        // no appropriate log append time we can generate at compaction time.\n        TimestampType timestampType = originalBatch.timestampType() == TimestampType.NO_TIMESTAMP_TYPE ?\n                TimestampType.CREATE_TIME : originalBatch.timestampType();\n        long logAppendTime = timestampType == TimestampType.LOG_APPEND_TIME ?\n                originalBatch.maxTimestamp() : RecordBatch.NO_TIMESTAMP;\n        long baseOffset = originalBatch.magic() >= RecordBatch.MAGIC_VALUE_V2 ?\n                originalBatch.baseOffset() : retainedRecords.get(0).offset();\n\n        // Convert records with older record versions to the current one\n        MemoryRecordsBuilder builder = new MemoryRecordsBuilder(bufferOutputStream, RecordBatch.CURRENT_MAGIC_VALUE,\n                compression, timestampType, baseOffset, logAppendTime, originalBatch.producerId(),\n                originalBatch.producerEpoch(), originalBatch.baseSequence(), originalBatch.isTransactional(),\n                originalBatch.isControlBatch(), originalBatch.partitionLeaderEpoch(), bufferOutputStream.limit(), deleteHorizonMs);\n\n        for (Record record : retainedRecords)\n            builder.append(record);\n\n        if (originalBatch.magic() >= RecordBatch.MAGIC_VALUE_V2)\n            // we must preserve the last offset from the initial batch in order to ensure that the\n            // last sequence number from the batch remains even after compaction. Otherwise, the producer\n            // could incorrectly see an out of sequence error.\n            builder.overrideLastOffset(originalBatch.lastOffset());\n\n        return builder;\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Get a duplicate of the byte buffer that backs this instance.\n     *\n     * <p><b>Position Independence:</b> Returning a duplicate ensures that position/limit\n     * changes made by callers do not affect the internal buffer position.</p>\n     *\n     * @return A {@link ByteBuffer} duplicate containing this record set\n     */\n    public ByteBuffer buffer() {\n        return buffer.duplicate();\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Create a {@code MemoryRecords} view containing a slice of this buffer.\n     *\n     * <p><b>Zero-Copy:</b> The returned instance shares the underlying buffer; no data is copied.</p>\n     *\n     * <p><b>Boundary Conditions:</b> The slice may start or end in the middle of a record batch.\n     * Callers must be aware that {@link #validBytes()} may differ from the slice size.</p>\n     *\n     * @param position The starting position in this buffer (0-based, inclusive)\n     * @param size The number of bytes to include in the slice\n     * @return A new {@code MemoryRecords} instance backed by the sliced buffer\n     * @throws IllegalArgumentException If position or size are invalid\n     */\n    @Override\n    public MemoryRecords slice(int position, int size) {\n        if (position < 0)\n            throw new IllegalArgumentException(\"Invalid position: \" + position + \" in read from \" + this);\n        if (position > buffer.limit())\n            throw new IllegalArgumentException(\"Slice from position \" + position + \" exceeds end position of \" + this);\n        if (size < 0)\n            throw new IllegalArgumentException(\"Invalid size: \" + size + \" in read from \" + this);\n\n        int availableBytes = Math.min(size, buffer.limit() - position);\n        // As of now, clients module support Java11 hence can't use ByteBuffer::slice(position, size) method.\n        // So we need to create a duplicate buffer and set the position and limit. Duplicate buffer\n        // is backed by original bytes hence not the content but only the relative position and limit\n        // are changed in the duplicate buffer. Once the position and limit are set, we can call the\n        // slice method to get the sliced buffer, which is a backed by the original buffer with the\n        // position reset to 0 and limit set to the size of the slice.\n        ByteBuffer slicedBuffer = buffer.duplicate();\n        slicedBuffer.position(position);\n        slicedBuffer.limit(position + availableBytes);\n        // Reset the position to 0 so that the sliced view has a relative position.\n        slicedBuffer = slicedBuffer.slice();\n\n        return readableRecords(slicedBuffer);\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public Iterable<MutableRecordBatch> batches() {\n        return batches;\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public String toString() {\n        return \"MemoryRecords(size=\" + sizeInBytes() +\n                \", buffer=\" + buffer +\n                \")\";\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public boolean equals(Object o) {\n        if (this == o)\n            return true;\n        if (o == null || getClass() != o.getClass())\n            return false;\n\n        MemoryRecords that = (MemoryRecords) o;\n\n        return buffer.equals(that.buffer);\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public int hashCode() {\n        return buffer.hashCode();\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Abstract base class for filtering record batches and individual records during log compaction.\n     *\n     * <p><b>Filtering Levels:</b>\n     * <ol>\n     *   <li>{@link #checkBatchRetention(RecordBatch)} — decides if an entire batch should be deleted\n     *       without examining records. This is useful for optimizing deletion of large batches.</li>\n     *   <li>{@link #shouldRetainRecord(RecordBatch, Record)} — decides if individual records\n     *       should be retained (e.g., based on TTL, topic configuration, or record key).</li>\n     * </ol>\n     * </p>\n     *\n     * <p><b>Compaction Semantics:</b> The filter is called during log compaction to:\n     * <ul>\n     *   <li>Discard stale records (those with earlier versions of the same key)</li>\n     *   <li>Enforce retention policies (delete records older than a TTL)</li>\n     *   <li>Clean up tombstones and transaction markers</li>\n     *   <li>Up-convert old message formats to the current version</li>\n     * </ul>\n     * </p>\n     *\n     * @see FilterResult\n     */\n    public abstract static class RecordFilter {\n        /** The current time used for TTL calculations, in milliseconds since epoch. */\n        public final long currentTime;\n        /** The number of milliseconds to retain tombstones and transaction markers. */\n        public final long deleteRetentionMs;\n\n        /**\n         * Construct a filter with the given time parameters.\n         *\n         * @param currentTime The current time in milliseconds since epoch\n         * @param deleteRetentionMs The minimum duration to retain deletion markers\n         */\n        public RecordFilter(final long currentTime, final long deleteRetentionMs) {\n            this.currentTime = currentTime;\n            this.deleteRetentionMs = deleteRetentionMs;\n        }\n\n        /**\n         * Result of batch-level retention check.\n         */\n        public static class BatchRetentionResult {\n            /** The batch retention decision. */\n            public final BatchRetention batchRetention;\n            /** Whether this batch contains an end-of-transaction marker for an empty transaction. */\n            public final boolean containsMarkerForEmptyTxn;\n\n            /**\n             * Construct a batch retention result.\n             *\n             * @param batchRetention The retention decision\n             * @param containsMarkerForEmptyTxn Whether the batch contains an empty transaction marker\n             */\n            public BatchRetentionResult(final BatchRetention batchRetention,\n                                        final boolean containsMarkerForEmptyTxn) {\n                this.batchRetention = batchRetention;\n                this.containsMarkerForEmptyTxn = containsMarkerForEmptyTxn;\n            }\n        }\n\n        /**\n         * Decision enum for batch-level retention.\n         */\n        public enum BatchRetention {\n            /** Delete the batch entirely without inspecting records. */\n            DELETE,\n            /** Retain the batch even if it is empty. */\n            RETAIN_EMPTY,\n            /** Delete the batch only if it becomes empty after filtering. */\n            DELETE_EMPTY\n        }\n\n        /**\n         * Check whether the full batch can be discarded without inspecting individual records.\n         *\n         * <p><b>Optimization:</b> This method is called first and avoids iteration overhead for\n         * batches that can be entirely discarded (e.g., all records are too old).</p>\n         *\n         * @param batch The {@link RecordBatch} to evaluate\n         * @return A {@link BatchRetentionResult} indicating the decision\n         */\n        protected abstract BatchRetentionResult checkBatchRetention(RecordBatch batch);\n\n        /**\n         * Check whether a record should be retained in the log.\n         *\n         * <p><b>Invocation:</b> This method is called only for records in batches that were not\n         * entirely discarded by {@link #checkBatchRetention(RecordBatch)}.</p>\n         *\n         * <p><b>Example Logic:</b> A real implementation might check:\n         * <ul>\n         *   <li>Record key uniqueness (keep only the latest version)</li>\n         *   <li>Record age (discard records older than the log retention period)</li>\n         *   <li>Tombstone retention (keep tombstones for a grace period to ensure eventual consistency)</li>\n         * </ul>\n         * </p>\n         *\n         * @param recordBatch The {@link RecordBatch} containing the record\n         * @param record The {@link Record} to evaluate\n         * @return {@code true} if the record should be kept, {@code false} if it should be discarded\n         */\n        protected abstract boolean shouldRetainRecord(RecordBatch recordBatch, Record record);\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Result of filtering a set of record batches.\n     *\n     * <p>This class summarizes the input/output metrics of the filtering operation,\n     * useful for logging and monitoring compaction progress.</p>\n     */\n    public static class FilterResult {\n        /** The output buffer containing filtered records. May be reallocated if insufficient capacity. */\n        private ByteBuffer outputBuffer;\n        /** Total number of records (messages) read during filtering. */\n        private int messagesRead = 0;\n        /** Total number of bytes read from input batches. */\n        private int bytesRead = 0;\n        /** Total number of records retained in the output. */\n        private int messagesRetained = 0;\n        /** Total number of bytes written to the output buffer. */\n        private int bytesRetained = 0;\n        /** The maximum offset of any retained record. */\n        private long maxOffset = -1L;\n        /** The maximum timestamp of any retained record. */\n        private long maxTimestamp = RecordBatch.NO_TIMESTAMP;\n        /** The offset of the record with the maximum timestamp (at a shallow level). */\n        private long shallowOffsetOfMaxTimestamp = -1L;\n\n        /**\n         * Construct a filter result with the given output buffer.\n         *\n         * @param outputBuffer The {@link ByteBuffer} to accumulate filtered records in\n         */\n        private FilterResult(ByteBuffer outputBuffer) {\n            this.outputBuffer = outputBuffer;\n        }\n\n        private void updateRetainedBatchMetadata(MutableRecordBatch retainedBatch, int numMessagesInBatch, boolean headerOnly) {\n            int bytesRetained = headerOnly ? DefaultRecordBatch.RECORD_BATCH_OVERHEAD : retainedBatch.sizeInBytes();\n            updateRetainedBatchMetadata(retainedBatch.maxTimestamp(), retainedBatch.lastOffset(),\n                    retainedBatch.lastOffset(), numMessagesInBatch, bytesRetained);\n        }\n\n        private void updateRetainedBatchMetadata(long maxTimestamp, long shallowOffsetOfMaxTimestamp, long maxOffset,\n                                                 int messagesRetained, int bytesRetained) {\n            validateBatchMetadata(maxTimestamp, shallowOffsetOfMaxTimestamp, maxOffset);\n            if (maxTimestamp > this.maxTimestamp) {\n                this.maxTimestamp = maxTimestamp;\n                this.shallowOffsetOfMaxTimestamp = shallowOffsetOfMaxTimestamp;\n            }\n            this.maxOffset = Math.max(maxOffset, this.maxOffset);\n            this.messagesRetained += messagesRetained;\n            this.bytesRetained += bytesRetained;\n        }\n\n        private void validateBatchMetadata(long maxTimestamp, long shallowOffsetOfMaxTimestamp, long maxOffset) {\n            if (maxTimestamp != RecordBatch.NO_TIMESTAMP && shallowOffsetOfMaxTimestamp < 0)\n                throw new IllegalArgumentException(\"shallowOffset undefined for maximum timestamp \" + maxTimestamp);\n            if (maxOffset < 0)\n                throw new IllegalArgumentException(\"maxOffset undefined\");\n        }\n\n        /**\n         * Get the output buffer containing filtered records.\n         *\n         * @return The {@link ByteBuffer} with filtered records\n         */\n        public ByteBuffer outputBuffer() {\n            return outputBuffer;\n        }\n\n        /**\n         * Get the total number of records read during filtering.\n         *\n         * @return The count of input records examined\n         */\n        public int messagesRead() {\n            return messagesRead;\n        }\n\n        /**\n         * Get the total number of bytes read from input batches.\n         *\n         * @return The count of input bytes\n         */\n        public int bytesRead() {\n            return bytesRead;\n        }\n\n        /**\n         * Get the total number of records retained in the output.\n         *\n         * @return The count of output records\n         */\n        public int messagesRetained() {\n            return messagesRetained;\n        }\n\n        /**\n         * Get the total number of bytes written to the output buffer.\n         *\n         * @return The count of output bytes\n         */\n        public int bytesRetained() {\n            return bytesRetained;\n        }\n\n        /**\n         * Get the maximum offset of any retained record.\n         *\n         * @return The highest offset, or -1L if no records were retained\n         */\n        public long maxOffset() {\n            return maxOffset;\n        }\n\n        /**\n         * Get the maximum timestamp of any retained record.\n         *\n         * @return The highest timestamp value\n         */\n        public long maxTimestamp() {\n            return maxTimestamp;\n        }\n\n        /**\n         * Get the offset of the record with the maximum timestamp.\n         *\n         * @return The offset at the maximum timestamp, or -1L if none\n         */\n        public long shallowOffsetOfMaxTimestamp() {\n            return shallowOffsetOfMaxTimestamp;\n        }\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Create a {@code MemoryRecords} instance wrapping the given buffer.\n     *\n     * <p>This factory method is the standard way to create a read-only view of serialized record batches.</p>\n     *\n     * @param buffer A {@link ByteBuffer} containing one or more serialized record batches\n     * @return A {@code MemoryRecords} instance backed by the buffer\n     */\n    public static MemoryRecords readableRecords(ByteBuffer buffer) {\n        return new MemoryRecords(buffer);\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Create a builder for writing records with default settings.\n     *\n     * <p><b>Defaults:</b>\n     * <ul>\n     *   <li>Magic version: {@link RecordBatch#CURRENT_MAGIC_VALUE}</li>\n     *   <li>Base offset: as provided</li>\n     *   <li>Producer ID: {@link RecordBatch#NO_PRODUCER_ID}</li>\n     *   <li>Transactional: false</li>\n     * </ul>\n     * </p>\n     *\n     * @param buffer The destination {@link ByteBuffer}\n     * @param compression The {@link Compression} algorithm to use\n     * @param timestampType The {@link TimestampType}\n     * @param baseOffset The starting offset for records in this batch\n     * @return A {@link MemoryRecordsBuilder} for appending records\n     */\n    public static MemoryRecordsBuilder builder(ByteBuffer buffer,\n                                               Compression compression,\n                                               TimestampType timestampType,\n                                               long baseOffset) {\n        return builder(buffer, RecordBatch.CURRENT_MAGIC_VALUE, compression, timestampType, baseOffset);\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Create a builder with a maximum batch size constraint.\n     *\n     * @param buffer The destination {@link ByteBuffer}\n     * @param compression The {@link Compression} algorithm\n     * @param timestampType The {@link TimestampType}\n     * @param baseOffset The starting offset\n     * @param maxSize The maximum size in bytes for the output batch; builder may stop early if exceeded\n     * @return A {@link MemoryRecordsBuilder} for appending records\n     */\n    public static MemoryRecordsBuilder builder(ByteBuffer buffer,\n                                               Compression compression,\n                                               TimestampType timestampType,\n                                               long baseOffset,\n                                               int maxSize) {\n        long logAppendTime = RecordBatch.NO_TIMESTAMP;\n        if (timestampType == TimestampType.LOG_APPEND_TIME)\n            logAppendTime = System.currentTimeMillis();\n\n        return new MemoryRecordsBuilder(buffer, RecordBatch.CURRENT_MAGIC_VALUE, compression, timestampType, baseOffset,\n            logAppendTime, RecordBatch.NO_PRODUCER_ID, RecordBatch.NO_PRODUCER_EPOCH, RecordBatch.NO_SEQUENCE,\n            false, false, RecordBatch.NO_PARTITION_LEADER_EPOCH, maxSize);\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Create a builder with custom magic version and log append time.\n     *\n     * @param buffer The destination {@link ByteBuffer}\n     * @param magic The record format version\n     * @param compression The {@link Compression} algorithm\n     * @param timestampType The {@link TimestampType}\n     * @param baseOffset The starting offset\n     * @param logAppendTime The timestamp to use for {@link TimestampType#LOG_APPEND_TIME}\n     * @return A {@link MemoryRecordsBuilder} for appending records\n     */\n    public static MemoryRecordsBuilder builder(ByteBuffer buffer,\n                                               byte magic,\n                                               Compression compression,\n                                               TimestampType timestampType,\n                                               long baseOffset,\n                                               long logAppendTime) {\n        return builder(buffer, magic, compression, timestampType, baseOffset, logAppendTime,\n                RecordBatch.NO_PRODUCER_ID, RecordBatch.NO_PRODUCER_EPOCH, RecordBatch.NO_SEQUENCE, false,\n                RecordBatch.NO_PARTITION_LEADER_EPOCH);\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Create a builder with custom magic version and auto-generated log append time if needed.\n     *\n     * @param buffer The destination {@link ByteBuffer}\n     * @param magic The record format version\n     * @param compression The {@link Compression} algorithm\n     * @param timestampType The {@link TimestampType}\n     * @param baseOffset The starting offset\n     * @return A {@link MemoryRecordsBuilder} for appending records\n     */\n    public static MemoryRecordsBuilder builder(ByteBuffer buffer,\n                                               byte magic,\n                                               Compression compression,\n                                               TimestampType timestampType,\n                                               long baseOffset) {\n        long logAppendTime = RecordBatch.NO_TIMESTAMP;\n        if (timestampType == TimestampType.LOG_APPEND_TIME)\n            logAppendTime = System.currentTimeMillis();\n        return builder(buffer, magic, compression, timestampType, baseOffset, logAppendTime,\n                RecordBatch.NO_PRODUCER_ID, RecordBatch.NO_PRODUCER_EPOCH, RecordBatch.NO_SEQUENCE, false,\n                RecordBatch.NO_PARTITION_LEADER_EPOCH);\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Create a builder with partition leader epoch.\n     *\n     * @param buffer The destination {@link ByteBuffer}\n     * @param magic The record format version\n     * @param compression The {@link Compression} algorithm\n     * @param timestampType The {@link TimestampType}\n     * @param baseOffset The starting offset\n     * @param logAppendTime The log append time\n     * @param partitionLeaderEpoch The current partition leader epoch\n     * @return A {@link MemoryRecordsBuilder} for appending records\n     */\n    public static MemoryRecordsBuilder builder(ByteBuffer buffer,\n                                               byte magic,\n                                               Compression compression,\n                                               TimestampType timestampType,\n                                               long baseOffset,\n                                               long logAppendTime,\n                                               int partitionLeaderEpoch) {\n        return builder(buffer, magic, compression, timestampType, baseOffset, logAppendTime,\n                RecordBatch.NO_PRODUCER_ID, RecordBatch.NO_PRODUCER_EPOCH, RecordBatch.NO_SEQUENCE, false, partitionLeaderEpoch);\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Create a builder for idempotent records.\n     *\n     * <p><b>Idempotence:</b> Records are marked with a producer ID, epoch, and base sequence\n     * to enable exactly-once semantics.</p>\n     *\n     * @param buffer The destination {@link ByteBuffer}\n     * @param compression The {@link Compression} algorithm\n     * @param baseOffset The starting offset\n     * @param producerId The producer's ID\n     * @param producerEpoch The producer's epoch\n     * @param baseSequence The starting sequence number\n     * @param isTransactional Whether these records are part of a transaction\n     * @return A {@link MemoryRecordsBuilder} for appending records\n     */\n    public static MemoryRecordsBuilder builder(ByteBuffer buffer,\n                                               Compression compression,\n                                               long baseOffset,\n                                               long producerId,\n                                               short producerEpoch,\n                                               int baseSequence,\n                                               boolean isTransactional) {\n        return builder(buffer, RecordBatch.CURRENT_MAGIC_VALUE, compression, TimestampType.CREATE_TIME, baseOffset,\n                RecordBatch.NO_TIMESTAMP, producerId, producerEpoch, baseSequence, isTransactional,\n                RecordBatch.NO_PARTITION_LEADER_EPOCH);\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Create a builder with producer information.\n     *\n     * @param buffer The destination {@link ByteBuffer}\n     * @param magic The record format version\n     * @param compression The {@link Compression} algorithm\n     * @param timestampType The {@link TimestampType}\n     * @param baseOffset The starting offset\n     * @param logAppendTime The log append time\n     * @param producerId The producer's ID\n     * @param producerEpoch The producer's epoch\n     * @param baseSequence The starting sequence number\n     * @return A {@link MemoryRecordsBuilder} for appending records\n     */\n    public static MemoryRecordsBuilder builder(ByteBuffer buffer,\n                                               byte magic,\n                                               Compression compression,\n                                               TimestampType timestampType,\n                                               long baseOffset,\n                                               long logAppendTime,\n                                               long producerId,\n                                               short producerEpoch,\n                                               int baseSequence) {\n        return builder(buffer, magic, compression, timestampType, baseOffset, logAppendTime,\n                producerId, producerEpoch, baseSequence, false, RecordBatch.NO_PARTITION_LEADER_EPOCH);\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Create a builder with full configuration.\n     *\n     * @param buffer The destination {@link ByteBuffer}\n     * @param magic The record format version\n     * @param compression The {@link Compression} algorithm\n     * @param timestampType The {@link TimestampType}\n     * @param baseOffset The starting offset\n     * @param logAppendTime The log append time\n     * @param producerId The producer's ID\n     * @param producerEpoch The producer's epoch\n     * @param baseSequence The starting sequence number\n     * @param isTransactional Whether records are transactional\n     * @param partitionLeaderEpoch The partition leader epoch\n     * @return A {@link MemoryRecordsBuilder} for appending records\n     */\n    public static MemoryRecordsBuilder builder(ByteBuffer buffer,\n                                               byte magic,\n                                               Compression compression,\n                                               TimestampType timestampType,\n                                               long baseOffset,\n                                               long logAppendTime,\n                                               long producerId,\n                                               short producerEpoch,\n                                               int baseSequence,\n                                               boolean isTransactional,\n                                               int partitionLeaderEpoch) {\n        return builder(buffer, magic, compression, timestampType, baseOffset,\n                logAppendTime, producerId, producerEpoch, baseSequence, isTransactional, false, partitionLeaderEpoch);\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Create a builder with control batch support.\n     *\n     * <p><b>Control Batches:</b> Used for transactional markers and coordination messages.</p>\n     *\n     * @param buffer The destination {@link ByteBuffer}\n     * @param magic The record format version\n     * @param compression The {@link Compression} algorithm\n     * @param timestampType The {@link TimestampType}\n     * @param baseOffset The starting offset\n     * @param logAppendTime The log append time\n     * @param producerId The producer's ID\n     * @param producerEpoch The producer's epoch\n     * @param baseSequence The starting sequence number\n     * @param isTransactional Whether records are transactional\n     * @param isControlBatch Whether this is a control batch\n     * @param partitionLeaderEpoch The partition leader epoch\n     * @return A {@link MemoryRecordsBuilder} for appending records\n     */\n    public static MemoryRecordsBuilder builder(ByteBuffer buffer,\n                                               byte magic,\n                                               Compression compression,\n                                               TimestampType timestampType,\n                                               long baseOffset,\n                                               long logAppendTime,\n                                               long producerId,\n                                               short producerEpoch,\n                                               int baseSequence,\n                                               boolean isTransactional,\n                                               boolean isControlBatch,\n                                               int partitionLeaderEpoch) {\n        return new MemoryRecordsBuilder(buffer, magic, compression, timestampType, baseOffset,\n                logAppendTime, producerId, producerEpoch, baseSequence, isTransactional, isControlBatch, partitionLeaderEpoch,\n                buffer.remaining());\n {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01JE9gJeQQg7HqokFMswTSda","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01VfHVPdpgkxMiv8N58QsT3T","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/documentation.md","content":"# Kafka Record Batch Serialization - Javadoc Enhancement\n\n## Overview\n\nThis document summarizes the comprehensive Javadoc additions made to three critical Kafka record serialization classes in `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/record/internal/`. These classes handle binary encoding and decoding of Kafka message batches, a fundamental component of the Kafka protocol.\n\n**Target Classes:**\n1. `RecordBatch.java` - Interface defining the contract for record batch access\n2. `DefaultRecordBatch.java` - Concrete implementation for magic v2 record format\n3. `MemoryRecords.java` - In-memory collection of serialized record batches\n\n---\n\n## Key Documentation Decisions\n\n### Thread Safety (Critical Requirement)\n\n**All classes explicitly document their thread-safety guarantees:**\n\n- **RecordBatch**: NOT thread-safe. Implementations are not synchronized; callers must provide external synchronization for concurrent access.\n- **DefaultRecordBatch**: NOT thread-safe. The underlying ByteBuffer is not synchronized. However, multiple threads may safely read from the same instance if the buffer is immutable.\n- **MemoryRecords**: NOT thread-safe for concurrent modification, but safe for concurrent reads if the underlying buffer is not being modified.\n\n**Rationale:** Thread safety is critical for correctness in Kafka, where batches are often shared across broker threads. Making this explicit prevents subtle bugs where callers assume thread-safety that doesn't exist.\n\n### Protocol Role Documentation\n\nEach class now includes explicit documentation of its role in the Kafka wire protocol:\n\n- **RecordBatch**: Defines the interface for accessing batch metadata (offsets, timestamps, compression, producer IDs) and iterating over contained records. Supports all magic versions (0, 1, 2+).\n- **DefaultRecordBatch**: Concrete implementation of magic v2 format with detailed schema documentation, CRC computation details, and compaction behavior.\n- **MemoryRecords**: Provides read-only access to sequences of serialized batches, typically from incoming produce requests or disk-based log segments.\n\n### Performance Characteristics\n\n**Critical Performance Notes Added:**\n\n1. **Lazy Decoding:** `streamingIterator()` enables memory-efficient decompression on-demand rather than loading entire decompressed streams.\n\n2. **Buffer Reuse:** Decompression buffer suppliers that reuse buffers across calls have \"significant performance impact\" - emphasized in multiple methods.\n\n3. **Offset/Timestamp Lookups:**\n   - `baseOffset()` may require deep iteration for magic v0-1; expensive\n   - `lastOffset()` is efficient for all magic versions\n   - `offsetOfMaxTimestamp()` requires full iteration over all records\n\n4. **Compression Handling:**\n   - `iterator()` fully decompresses into memory (simpler, resource-safe)\n   - `streamingIterator()` decompresses on-demand (lower memory footprint)\n   - `skipKeyValueIterator()` skips record data to reduce memory usage\n\n5. **CRC Computation:**\n   - Covers bytes from attributes field to end of batch\n   - O(n) in batch size; should not be called gratuitously\n   - Partition leader epoch intentionally excluded to allow in-place updates\n\n6. **Valid Bytes Calculation:**\n   - `validBytes()` is cached on first access\n   - Returns sum of complete batch sizes, excluding partial batches\n   - May differ from `sizeInBytes()` due to trailing incomplete data\n\n### Compaction and Sequence Preservation\n\n**DefaultRecordBatch** includes detailed documentation of compaction behavior:\n\n- Base and last offsets/sequences are preserved from original batches to maintain producer state\n- Empty batches can be retained to preserve producer sequence information\n- Base timestamp reflects first record (or delete horizon if set)\n- Max timestamp reflects current records (preserved after compaction for LOG_APPEND_TIME)\n- Delete horizon is automatically set for batches with tombstones/markers during filtering\n\n### Serialization Format\n\n**DefaultRecordBatch** includes complete binary schema documentation:\n\n```\nRecordBatch =>\n  BaseOffset => Int64\n  Length => Int32\n  PartitionLeaderEpoch => Int32\n  Magic => Int8\n  CRC => Uint32\n  Attributes => Int16\n  LastOffsetDelta => Int32\n  BaseTimestamp => Int64\n  MaxTimestamp => Int64\n  ProducerId => Int64\n  ProducerEpoch => Int16\n  BaseSequence => Int32\n  RecordsCount => Int32\n  Records => [Record]\n```\n\nWith detailed explanation of:\n- Field offsets and sizes (as static constants)\n- Attribute bit layout (compression, transactional, control, delete horizon, timestamp type)\n- CRC computation scope (why partition leader epoch is excluded)\n\n---\n\n## Class-Level Documentation Summary\n\n### RecordBatch Interface\n\n**Purpose & Role:**\n- Container for records in the Kafka log\n- Fundamental unit of serialization in Kafka wire protocol\n- Provides read-only access to batch metadata and records\n\n**Key Additions:**\n- Thread-safety: NOT thread-safe; requires external synchronization\n- Protocol role and magic version explanation\n- References to related classes via `{@link}` tags\n\n**Documented Constants:**\n- Magic versions (0, 1, 2)\n- Sentinel values (NO_TIMESTAMP, NO_PRODUCER_ID, NO_SEQUENCE, NO_PARTITION_LEADER_EPOCH)\n\n**Public Methods (34 methods):**\n- All methods now include `@return` and `@throws` tags where applicable\n- Performance notes for expensive operations (baseOffset, offsetOfMaxTimestamp, streamingIterator)\n- Compression handling semantics clearly explained\n- Offset/sequence delta behavior documented\n\n### DefaultRecordBatch\n\n**Purpose & Role:**\n- Concrete implementation of magic v2 record batch format\n- Handles binary serialization/deserialization with CRC-32C checksums\n- Supports compression, transactional markers, and control records\n- Mutable variant for in-place updates (setLastOffset, setMaxTimestamp)\n\n**Key Additions:**\n- Complete schema documentation with field offsets\n- CRC computation details and validation logic\n- Compaction behavior explanation\n- Performance characteristics for iterator variants\n\n**Field Constants (16 static constants):**\n- Position and length of each header field\n- Attribute bit masks\n- Overhead calculation constant\n\n**Public These classes handle binary encoding and decoding of Kafka message batches, a fundamental component of the Kafka protocol.\n\n**Target Classes:**\n1. `RecordBatch.java` - Interface defining the contract for record batch access\n2. `DefaultRecordBatch.java` - Concrete implementation for magic v2 record format\n3. `MemoryRecords.java` - In-memory collection of serialized record batches\n\n---\n\n## Key Documentation Decisions\n\n### Thread Safety (Critical Requirement)\n\n**All classes explicitly document their thread-safety guarantees:**\n\n- **RecordBatch**: NOT thread-safe. Implementations are not synchronized; callers must provide external synchronization for concurrent access.\n- **DefaultRecordBatch**: NOT thread-safe. The underlying ByteBuffer is not synchronized. However, multiple threads may safely read from the same instance if the buffer is immutable.\n- **MemoryRecords**: NOT thread-safe for concurrent modification, but safe for concurrent reads if the underlying buffer is not being modified.\n\n**Rationale:** Thread safety is critical for correctness in Kafka, where batches are often shared across broker threads. Making this explicit prevents subtle bugs where callers assume thread-safety that doesn't exist.\n\n### Protocol Role Documentation\n\nEach class now includes explicit documentation of its role in the Kafka wire protocol:\n\n- **RecordBatch**: Defines the interface for accessing batch metadata (offsets, timestamps, compression, producer IDs) and iterating over contained records. Supports all magic versions (0, 1, 2+).\n- **DefaultRecordBatch**: Concrete implementation of magic v2 format with detailed schema documentation, CRC computation details, and compaction behavior.\n- **MemoryRecords**: Provides read-only access to sequences of serialized batches, typically from incoming produce requests or disk-based log segments.\n\n### Performance Characteristics\n\n**Critical Performance Notes Added:**\n\n1. **Lazy Decoding:** `streamingIterator()` enables memory-efficient decompression on-demand rather than loading entire decompressed streams.\n\n2. **Buffer Reuse:** Decompression buffer suppliers that reuse buffers across calls have \"significant performance impact\" - emphasized in multiple methods.\n\n3. **Offset/Timestamp Lookups:**\n   - `baseOffset()` may require deep iteration for magic v0-1; expensive\n   - `lastOffset()` is efficient for all magic versions\n   - `offsetOfMaxTimestamp()` requires full iteration over all records\n\n4. **Compression Handling:**\n   - `iterator()` fully decompresses into memory (simpler, resource-safe)\n   - `streamingIterator()` decompresses on-demand (lower memory footprint)\n   - `skipKeyValueIterator()` skips record data to reduce memory usage\n\n5. **CRC Computation:**\n   - Covers bytes from attributes field to end of batch\n   - O(n) in batch size; should not be called gratuitously\n   - Partition leader epoch intentionally excluded to allow in-place updates\n\n6. **Valid Bytes Calculation:**\n   - `validBytes()` is cached on first access\n   - Returns sum of complete batch sizes, excluding partial batches\n   - May differ from `sizeInBytes()` due to trailing incomplete data\n\n### Compaction and Sequence Preservation\n\n**DefaultRecordBatch** includes detailed documentation of compaction behavior:\n\n- Base and last offsets/sequences are preserved from original batches to maintain producer state\n- Empty batches can be retained to preserve producer sequence information\n- Base timestamp reflects first record (or delete horizon if set)\n- Max timestamp reflects current records (preserved after compaction for LOG_APPEND_TIME)\n- Delete horizon is automatically set for batches with tombstones/markers during filtering\n\n### Serialization Format\n\n**DefaultRecordBatch** includes complete binary schema documentation:\n\n```\nRecordBatch =>\n  BaseOffset => Int64\n  Length => Int32\n  PartitionLeaderEpoch => Int32\n  Magic => Int8\n  CRC => Uint32\n  Attributes => Int16\n  LastOffsetDelta => Int32\n  BaseTimestamp => Int64\n  MaxTimestamp => Int64\n  ProducerId => Int64\n  ProducerEpoch => Int16\n  BaseSequence => Int32\n  RecordsCount => Int32\n  Records => [Record]\n```\n\nWith detailed explanation of:\n- Field offsets and sizes (as static constants)\n- Attribute bit layout (compression, transactional, control, delete horizon, timestamp type)\n- CRC computation scope (why partition leader epoch is excluded)\n\n---\n\n## Class-Level Documentation In old versions of the record format (versions 0 and 1),\n * a batch consisted always of a single record if no compression was enabled, but could contain\n * many records otherwise. Newer versions (magic versions 2 and above) will generally contain many records\n * regardless of compression.\n */\npublic interface RecordBatch extends Iterable<Record> {\n```\n\n### AFTER:\n```java\n/**\n * A record batch is a container for records. In old versions of the record format (versions 0 and 1),\n * a batch consisted always of a single record if no compression was enabled, but could contain\n * many records otherwise. Newer versions (magic versions 2 and above) will generally contain many records\n * regardless of compression.\n *\n * <p><b>Thread Safety:</b> {@code RecordBatch} implementations are <b>not thread-safe</b>.\n * Callers must ensure external synchronization when accessing a batch from multiple threads.\n * However, multiple independent batches can be safely accessed concurrently.</p>\n *\n * <p><b>Protocol Role:</b> In the Kafka wire protocol, record batches are the fundamental unit of serialization.\n * Each batch contains a header with metadata (magic version, compression type, timestamps, offsets, producer ID, etc.)\n * followed by the actual record data. This interface provides read-only access to batch metadata and records,\n * allowing consumers and brokers to parse and iterate over log entries.</p>\n *\n * <p><b>Magic Versions:</b>\n * <ul>\n *   <li>Magic 0-1: Legacy format with limited metadata; single record if uncompressed</li>\n *   <li>Magic 2+: Current format with rich metadata; multiple records per batch</li>\n * </ul>\n * </p>\n */\npublic interface RecordBatch extends Iterable<Record> {\n```\n\n---\n\n## Example 2: RecordBatch Method Documentation\n\n### BEFORE:\n```java\n/**\n * Get the record format version of this record batch (i.e its magic value).\n *\n * @return the magic byte\n */\nbyte magic();\n```\n\n### AFTER:\n```java\n/**\n * Get the record format version of this record batch (i.e. its magic value).\n *\n * <p>The magic value determines the binary format of the batch header and records within it.\n * Common values are 0 (legacy), 1 (legacy), and 2 (current/recommended).</p>\n *\n * @return The magic byte indicating the record format version\n */\nbyte magic();\n```\n\n---\n\n## Example 3: Complex Method with Performance Notes\n\n### BEFORE:\n```java\n/**\n * Return a streaming iterator which basically delays decompression of the record stream until the records\n * are actually asked for using {@link Iterator#next()}. If the message format does not support streaming\n * iteration, then the normal iterator is returned. Either way, callers should ensure that the iterator is closed.\n *\n * @param decompressionBufferSupplier The supplier of ByteBuffer(s) used for decompression if supported.\n *                                    For small record batches, allocating a potentially large buffer (64 KB for LZ4)\n *                                    will dominate the cost of decompressing and iterating over the records in the\n *                                    batch. As such, a supplier that reuses buffers will have a significant\n *                                    performance impact.\n * @return The closeable iterator\n */\nCloseableIterator<Record> streamingIterator(BufferSupplier decompressionBufferSupplier);\n```\n\n### AFTER:\n```java\n/**\n * Return a streaming iterator which delays decompression of the record stream until records\n * are actually requested using {@link Iterator#next()}.\n *\n * <p><b>Performance Note:</b> For compressed batches, this enables memory-efficient iteration\n * by decompressing data on-demand rather than loading the entire decompressed stream into memory.\n * The buffer supplier parameter allows callers to reuse decompression buffers, which is\n * critical for performance. For small batches (< 64KB), allocating a large buffer (e.g., 64 KB for LZ4)\n * can dominate the cost of decompression.</p>\n *\n * <p><b>Resource Management:</b> The returned iterator must be closed to release decompression\n * resources. Consider using try-with-resources.</p>\n *\n * @param decompressionBufferSupplier The supplier of {@link ByteBuffer}s used for decompression\n *                                    if the batch is compressed. Suppliers that reuse buffers across\n *                                    iterations have significant performance impact.\n * @return A {@link CloseableIterator} over {@link Record}s in this batch; must be closed by caller\n */\nCloseableIterator<Record> streamingIterator(BufferSupplier decompressionBufferSupplier);\n```\n\n---\n\n## Example 4: DefaultRecordBatch Class Documentation\n\n### BEFORE:\n```java\n/**\n * RecordBatch implementation for magic 2 and above. The schema is given below:\n *\n * RecordBatch =>\n *  BaseOffset => Int64\n *  Length => Int32\n *  PartitionLeaderEpoch => Int32\n *  Magic => Int8\n *  CRC => Uint32\n *  ...\n * (schema continues)\n */\npublic class DefaultRecordBatch extends AbstractRecordBatch implements MutableRecordBatch {\n```\n\n### AFTER:\n```java\n/**\n * {@link RecordBatch} implementation for the Kafka magic version 2 (and above) record format.\n *\n * <p><b>Thread Safety:</b> {@code DefaultRecordBatch} instances are <b>not thread-safe</b>.\n * The underlying {@link ByteBuffer} is not synchronized. Callers must ensure external synchronization\n * or create separate instances if multiple threads need concurrent access. However, since batches are\n * typically read-only after creation, sharing immutable batch instances across threads is safe.</p>\n *\n * <p><b>Binary Format:</b> The v2 record batch consists of a fixed header (56 bytes) followed by\n * variable-length record data. The CRC covers all bytes after the magic byte, including attributes,\n * timestamps, producer IDs, sequence numbers, and record data. The partition leader epoch is\n * intentionally excluded from the CRC to allow brokers to update it in-place without recomputation.</p>\n *\n * <p><b>Schema:</b>\n * <pre>{@code\n *   RecordBatch =>\n *     BaseOffset => Int64\n *     Length => Int32\n *     PartitionLeaderEpoch => Int32\n *     Magic => Int8\n *     CRC => Uint32\n *     Attributes => Int16\n *     LastOffsetDelta => Int32\n *     BaseTimestamp => Int64\n *     MaxTimestamp => Int64\n *     ProducerId => Int64\n *     ProducerEpoch => Int16\n *     BaseSequence => Int32\n *     RecordsCount => Int32\n *     Records => [Record]\n * }</pre>\n * </p>\n *\n * <p><b>Compression:</b> When compression is enabled, the compressed record data immediately\n * follows the record count field. Decompression is handled transparently by {@link #streamingIterator}\n * and related methods.</p>\n *\n * <p><b>Compaction Behavior:</b> During log compaction, the base and last offsets/sequences are\n * preserved from the original batch to maintain producer state integrity. This ensures that after\n * a broker restart, the producer's expected next sequence number remains in sync with the broker's\n * state, preventing spurious OutOfOrderSequence errors.</p>\n *\n * <p><b>Attributes:</b> The 16-bit attributes field encodes compression type, timestamp type,\n * transactional flag, control flag, and delete horizon flag. The upper 10 bits are currently unused\n * and must be zero for forward compatibility.</p>\n *\n * @see RecordBatch\n * @see MutableRecordBatch\n * @see MemoryRecords\n */\npublic class DefaultRecordBatch extends AbstractRecordBatch implements MutableRecordBatch {\n```\n\n---\n\n## Example 5: Static Builder Method Documentation\n\n### BEFORE:\n```java\npublic static MemoryRecordsBuilder builder(ByteBuffer buffer,\n                                           Compression compression,\n                                           TimestampType timestampType,\n                                           long baseOffset) {\n    return builder(buffer, RecordBatch.CURRENT_MAGIC_VALUE, compression, timestampType, baseOffset);\n}\n```\n\n### AFTER:\n```java\n/**\n * Create a builder for writing records with default settings.\n *\n * <p><b>Defaults:</b>\n * <ul>\n *   <li>Magic version: {@link RecordBatch#CURRENT_MAGIC_VALUE}</li>\n *   <li>Base offset: as provided</li>\n *   <li>Producer ID: {@link RecordBatch#NO_PRODUCER_ID}</li>\n *   <li>Transactional: false</li>\n * </ul>\n * </p>\n *\n * @param buffer The destination {@link ByteBuffer}\n * @param compression The {@link Compression} algorithm to use\n * @param timestampType The {@link TimestampType}\n * @param baseOffset The starting offset for records in this batch\n * @return A {@link MemoryRecordsBuilder} for appending records\n */\npublic static MemoryRecordsBuilder builder(ByteBuffer buffer,\n                                           Compression compression,\n                                           TimestampType timestampType,\n                                           long baseOffset) {\n    return builder(buffer, RecordBatch.CURRENT_MAGIC_VALUE, compression, timestampType, baseOffset);\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Example 6: RecordFilter Documentation (Nested Class)\n\n### BEFORE:\n```java\npublic abstract static class RecordFilter {\n    public final long currentTime;\n    public final long deleteRetentionMs;\n\n    public RecordFilter(final long currentTime, final long deleteRetentionMs) {\n        this.currentTime = currentTime;\n        this.deleteRetentionMs = deleteRetentionMs;\n    }\n\n    protected abstract BatchRetentionResult checkBatchRetention(RecordBatch batch);\n\n    protected abstract boolean shouldRetainRecord(RecordBatch recordBatch, Record record);\n}\n```\n\n### AFTER:\n```java\n/**\n * Abstract base class for filtering record batches and individual records during log compaction.\n *\n * <p><b>Filtering Levels:</b>\n * <ol>\n *   <li>{@link #checkBatchRetention(RecordBatch)} — decides if an entire batch should be deleted\n *       without examining records. This is useful for optimizing deletion of large batches.</li>\n *   <li>{@link #shouldRetainRecord(RecordBatch, Record)} — decides if individual records\n *       should be retained (e.g., based on TTL, topic configuration, or record key).</li>\n * </ol>\n * </p>\n *\n * <p><b>Compaction Semantics:</b> The filter is called during log compaction to:\n * <ul>\n *   <li>Discard stale records (those with earlier versions of the same key)</li>\n *   <li>Enforce retention policies (delete records older than a TTL)</li>\n *   <li>Clean up tombstones and transaction markers</li>\n *   <li>Up-convert old message formats to the current version</li>\n * </ul>\n * </p>\n *\n * @see FilterResult\n */\npublic abstract static class RecordFilter {\n    /** The current time used for TTL calculations, in milliseconds since epoch. */\n    public final long currentTime;\n    /** The number of milliseconds to retain tombstones and transaction markers. */\n    public final long deleteRetentionMs;\n\n    /**\n     * Construct a filter with the given time parameters.\n     *\n     * @param currentTime The current time in milliseconds since epoch\n     * @param deleteRetentionMs The minimum duration to retain deletion markers\n     */\n    public RecordFilter(final long currentTime, final long deleteRetentionMs) {\n        this.currentTime = currentTime;\n        this.deleteRetentionMs = deleteRetentionMs;\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Check whether the full batch can be discarded without inspecting individual records.\n     *\n     * <p><b>Optimization:</b> This method is called first and avoids iteration overhead for\n     * batches that can be entirely discarded (e.g., all records are too old).</p>\n     *\n     * @param batch The {@link RecordBatch} to evaluate\n     * @return A {@link BatchRetentionResult} indicating the decision\n     */\n    protected abstract BatchRetentionResult checkBatchRetention(RecordBatch batch);\n\n    /**\n     * Check whether a record should be retained in the log.\n     *\n     * <p><b>Invocation:</b> This method is called only for records in batches that were not\n     * entirely discarded by {@link #checkBatchRetention(RecordBatch)}.</p>\n     *\n     * <p><b>Example Logic:</b> A real implementation might check:\n     * <ul>\n     *   <li>Record key uniqueness (keep only the latest version)</li>\n     *   <li>Record age (discard records older than the log retention period)</li>\n     *   <li>Tombstone retention (keep tombstones for a grace period to ensure eventual consistency)</li>\n     * </ul>\n     * </p>\n     *\n     * @param recordBatch The {@link RecordBatch} containing the record\n     * @param record The {@link Record} to evaluate\n     * @return {@code true} if the record should be kept, {@code false} if it should be discarded\n     */\n    protected abstract boolean shouldRetainRecord(RecordBatch recordBatch, Record record);\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Example 7: Mutable Method Documentation\n\n### BEFORE:\n```java\n@Override\npublic void setMaxTimestamp(TimestampType timestampType, long maxTimestamp) {\n    long currentMaxTimestamp = maxTimestamp();\n    // We don't need to recompute crc if the timestamp is not updated.\n    if (timestampType() == timestampType && currentMaxTimestamp == maxTimestamp)\n        return;\n    // ... implementation ...\n}\n```\n\n### AFTER:\n```java\n/**\n * Modify the maximum timestamp and timestamp type of this batch.\n *\n * <p><b>Thread Safety:</b> This method is <b>not thread-safe</b>. Concurrent calls to mutation\n * methods or reads during mutation will produce undefined results.</p>\n *\n * <p><b>CRC Recomputation:</b> If the timestamp or timestamp type changes, the CRC is\n * automatically recomputed since both fields are covered by the checksum.</p>\n *\n * <p><b>Optimization:</b> If the new values match the current ones, no modification occurs\n * and CRC recomputation is skipped.</p>\n *\n * @param timestampType The new {@link TimestampType} for this batch\n * @param maxTimestamp The new maximum timestamp in milliseconds since epoch\n */\n@Override\npublic void setMaxTimestamp(TimestampType timestampType, long maxTimestamp) {\n    long currentMaxTimestamp = maxTimestamp();\n    // We don't need to recompute crc if the timestamp is not updated.\n    if (timestampType() == timestampType && currentMaxTimestamp == maxTimestamp)\n        return;\n    // ... implementation ...\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Summary of Improvements\n\nThe enhancements transform minimal documentation into comprehensive guides that cover:\n\n1. **Thread Safety** - Explicit guarantees and synchronization requirements\n2. **Protocol Details** - Binary format, field layouts, CRC computation\n3. **Performance** - Trade-offs, optimization opportunities, buffer reuse\n4. **Compaction** - Sequence preservation, tombstone handling, delete horizons\n5. **Filtering** - Retention decisions, use cases, examples\n6. **Cross-References** - {@link} tags connecting related classes\n7. **Use Cases** - In old versions of the record format (versions 0 and 1),\n * a batch consisted always of a single record if no compression was enabled, but could contain\n * many records otherwise. Newer versions (magic versions 2 and above) will generally contain many records\n * regardless of compression.\n */\npublic interface RecordBatch extends Iterable<Record> {\n```\n\n### AFTER:\n```java\n/**\n * A record batch is a container for records. In old versions of the record format (versions 0 and 1),\n * a batch consisted always of a single record if no compression was enabled, but could contain\n * many records otherwise. Newer versions (magic versions 2 and above) will generally contain many records\n * regardless of compression.\n *\n * <p><b>Thread Safety:</b> {@code RecordBatch} implementations are <b>not thread-safe</b>.\n * Callers must ensure external synchronization when accessing a batch from multiple threads.\n * However, multiple independent batches can be safely accessed concurrently.</p>\n *\n * <p><b>Protocol Role:</b> In the Kafka wire protocol, record batches are the fundamental unit of serialization.\n * Each batch contains a header with metadata (magic version, compression type, timestamps, offsets, producer ID, etc.)\n * followed by the actual record data. This interface provides read-only access to batch metadata and records,\n * allowing consumers and brokers to parse and iterate over log entries.</p>\n *\n * <p><b>Magic Versions:</b>\n * <ul>\n *   <li>Magic 0-1: Legacy format with limited metadata; single record if uncompressed</li>\n *   <li>Magic 2+: Current format with rich metadata; multiple records per batch</li>\n * </ul>\n * </p>\n */\npublic interface RecordBatch extends Iterable<Record> {\n```\n\n---\n\n## Example 2: RecordBatch Method Documentation\n\n### BEFORE:\n```java\n/**\n * Get the record format version of this record batch (i.e its magic value).\n *\n * @return the magic byte\n */\nbyte magic();\n```\n\n### AFTER:\n```java\n/**\n * Get the record format version of this record batch (i.e. its magic value).\n *\n * <p>The magic value determines the binary format of the batch header and records within it.\n * Common values are 0 (legacy), 1 (legacy), and 2 (current/recommended).</p>\n *\n * @return The magic byte indicating the record format version\n */\nbyte magic();\n```\n\n---\n\n## Example 3: Complex Method with Performance Notes\n\n### BEFORE:\n```java\n/**\n * Return a streaming iterator which basically delays decompression of the record stream until the records\n * are actually asked for using {@link Iterator#next()}. If the message format does not support streaming\n * iteration, then the normal iterator is returned. Either way, callers should ensure that the iterator is closed.\n *\n * @param decompressionBufferSupplier The supplier of ByteBuffer(s) used for decompression if supported.\n *                                    For small record batches, allocating a potentially large buffer (64 KB for LZ4)\n *                                    will dominate the cost of decompressing and iterating over the records in the\n *                                    batch. As such, a supplier that reuses buffers will have a significant\n *                                    performance impact.\n * @return The closeable iterator\n */\nCloseableIterator<Record> streamingIterator(BufferSupplier decompressionBufferSupplier);\n```\n\n### AFTER:\n```java\n/**\n * Return a streaming iterator which delays decompression of the record stream until records\n * are actually requested using {@link Iterator#next()}.\n *\n * <p><b>Performance Note:</b> For compressed batches, this enables memory-efficient iteration\n * by decompressing data on-demand rather than loading the entire decompressed stream into memory.\n * The buffer supplier parameter allows callers to reuse decompression buffers, which is\n * critical for performance. For small batches (< 64KB), allocating a large buffer (e.g., 64 KB for LZ4)\n * can dominate the cost of decompression.</p>\n *\n * <p><b>Resource Management:</b> The returned iterator must be closed to release decompression\n * resources.
