If the message format does not support streaming\n * iteration, then the normal iterator is returned. Either way, callers should ensure that the iterator is closed.\n *\n * @param decompressionBufferSupplier The supplier of ByteBuffer(s) used for decompression if supported.\n *                                    For small record batches, allocating a potentially large buffer (64 KB for LZ4)\n *                                    will dominate the cost of decompressing and iterating over the records in the\n *                                    batch. As such, a supplier that reuses buffers will have a significant\n *                                    performance impact.\n * @return The closeable iterator\n */\nCloseableIterator<Record> streamingIterator(BufferSupplier decompressionBufferSupplier);\n```\n\n### AFTER:\n```java\n/**\n * Return a streaming iterator which delays decompression of the record stream until records\n * are actually requested using {@link Iterator#next()}.\n *\n * <p><b>Performance Note:</b> For compressed batches, this enables memory-efficient iteration\n * by decompressing data on-demand rather than loading the entire decompressed stream into memory.\n * The buffer supplier parameter allows callers to reuse decompression buffers, which is\n * critical for performance. For small batches (< 64KB), allocating a large buffer (e.g., 64 KB for LZ4)\n * can dominate the cost of decompression.</p>\n *\n * <p><b>Resource Management:</b> The returned iterator must be closed to release decompression\n * resources. Consider using try-with-resources.</p>\n *\n * @param decompressionBufferSupplier The supplier of {@link ByteBuffer}s used for decompression\n *                                    if the batch is compressed. Suppliers that reuse buffers across\n *                                    iterations have significant performance impact.\n * @return A {@link CloseableIterator} over {@link Record}s in this batch; must be closed by caller\n */\nCloseableIterator<Record> streamingIterator(BufferSupplier decompressionBufferSupplier);\n```\n\n---\n\n## Example 4: DefaultRecordBatch Class Documentation\n\n### BEFORE:\n```java\n/**\n * RecordBatch implementation for magic 2 and above. The schema is given below:\n *\n * RecordBatch =>\n *  BaseOffset => Int64\n *  Length => Int32\n *  PartitionLeaderEpoch => Int32\n *  Magic => Int8\n *  CRC => Uint32\n *  ...\n * (schema continues)\n */\npublic class DefaultRecordBatch extends AbstractRecordBatch implements MutableRecordBatch {\n```\n\n### AFTER:\n```java\n/**\n * {@link RecordBatch} implementation for the Kafka magic version 2 (and above) record format.\n *\n * <p><b>Thread Safety:</b> {@code DefaultRecordBatch} instances are <b>not thread-safe</b>.\n * The underlying {@link ByteBuffer} is not synchronized. Callers must ensure external synchronization\n * or create separate instances if multiple threads need concurrent access. However, since batches are\n * typically read-only after creation, sharing immutable batch instances across threads is safe.</p>\n *\n * <p><b>Binary Format:</b> The v2 record batch consists of a fixed header (56 bytes) followed by\n * variable-length record data. The CRC covers all bytes after the magic byte, including attributes,\n * timestamps, producer IDs, sequence numbers, and record data. The partition leader epoch is\n * intentionally excluded from the CRC to allow brokers to update it in-place without recomputation.</p>\n *\n * <p><b>Schema:</b>\n * <pre>{@code\n *   RecordBatch =>\n *     BaseOffset => Int64\n *     Length => Int32\n *     PartitionLeaderEpoch => Int32\n *     Magic => Int8\n *     CRC => Uint32\n *     Attributes => Int16\n *     LastOffsetDelta => Int32\n *     BaseTimestamp => Int64\n *     MaxTimestamp => Int64\n *     ProducerId => Int64\n *     ProducerEpoch => Int16\n *     BaseSequence => Int32\n *     RecordsCount => Int32\n *     Records => [Record]\n * }</pre>\n * </p>\n *\n * <p><b>Compression:</b> When compression is enabled, the compressed record data immediately\n * follows the record count field. Decompression is handled transparently by {@link #streamingIterator}\n * and related methods.</p>\n *\n * <p><b>Compaction Behavior:</b> During log compaction, the base and last offsets/sequences are\n * preserved from the original batch to maintain producer state integrity. This ensures that after\n * a broker restart, the producer's expected next sequence number remains in sync with the broker's\n * state, preventing spurious OutOfOrderSequence errors.</p>\n *\n * <p><b>Attributes:</b> The 16-bit attributes field encodes compression type, timestamp type,\n * transactional flag, control flag, and delete horizon flag. The upper 10 bits are currently unused\n * and must be zero for forward compatibility.</p>\n *\n * @see RecordBatch\n * @see MutableRecordBatch\n * @see MemoryRecords\n */\npublic class DefaultRecordBatch extends AbstractRecordBatch implements MutableRecordBatch {\n```\n\n---\n\n## Example 5: Static Builder Method Documentation\n\n### BEFORE:\n```java\npublic static MemoryRecordsBuilder builder(ByteBuffer buffer,\n                                           Compression compression,\n                                           TimestampType timestampType,\n                                           long baseOffset) {\n    return builder(buffer, RecordBatch.CURRENT_MAGIC_VALUE, compression, timestampType, baseOffset);\n}\n```\n\n### AFTER:\n```java\n/**\n * Create a builder for writing records with default settings.\n *\n * <p><b>Defaults:</b>\n * <ul>\n *   <li>Magic version: {@link RecordBatch#CURRENT_MAGIC_VALUE}</li>\n *   <li>Base offset: as provided</li>\n *   <li>Producer ID: {@link RecordBatch#NO_PRODUCER_ID}</li>\n *   <li>Transactional: false</li>\n * </ul>\n * </p>\n *\n * @param buffer The destination {@link ByteBuffer}\n * @param compression The {@link Compression} algorithm to use\n * @param timestampType The {@link TimestampType}\n * @param baseOffset The starting offset for records in this batch\n * @return A {@link MemoryRecordsBuilder} for appending records\n */\npublic static MemoryRecordsBuilder builder(ByteBuffer buffer,\n                                           Compression compression,\n                                           TimestampType timestampType,\n                                           long baseOffset) {\n    return builder(buffer, RecordBatch.CURRENT_MAGIC_VALUE, compression, timestampType, baseOffset);\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Example 6: RecordFilter Documentation (Nested Class)\n\n### BEFORE:\n```java\npublic abstract static class RecordFilter {\n    public final long currentTime;\n    public final long deleteRetentionMs;\n\n    public RecordFilter(final long currentTime, final long deleteRetentionMs) {\n        this.currentTime = currentTime;\n        this.deleteRetentionMs = deleteRetentionMs;\n    }\n\n    protected abstract BatchRetentionResult checkBatchRetention(RecordBatch batch);\n\n    protected abstract boolean shouldRetainRecord(RecordBatch recordBatch, Record record);\n}\n```\n\n### AFTER:\n```java\n/**\n * Abstract base class for filtering record batches and individual records during log compaction.\n *\n * <p><b>Filtering Levels:</b>\n * <ol>\n *   <li>{@link #checkBatchRetention(RecordBatch)} — decides if an entire batch should be deleted\n *       without examining records. This is useful for optimizing deletion of large batches.</li>\n *   <li>{@link #shouldRetainRecord(RecordBatch, Record)} — decides if individual records\n *       should be retained (e.g., based on TTL, topic configuration, or record key).</li>\n * </ol>\n * </p>\n *\n * <p><b>Compaction Semantics:</b> The filter is called during log compaction to:\n * <ul>\n *   <li>Discard stale records (those with earlier versions of the same key)</li>\n *   <li>Enforce retention policies (delete records older than a TTL)</li>\n *   <li>Clean up tombstones and transaction markers</li>\n *   <li>Up-convert old message formats to the current version</li>\n * </ul>\n * </p>\n *\n * @see FilterResult\n */\npublic abstract static class RecordFilter {\n    /** The current time used for TTL calculations, in milliseconds since epoch. */\n    public final long currentTime;\n    /** The number of milliseconds to retain tombstones and transaction markers. */\n    public final long deleteRetentionMs;\n\n    /**\n     * Construct a filter with the given time parameters.\n     *\n     * @param currentTime The current time in milliseconds since epoch\n     * @param deleteRetentionMs The minimum duration to retain deletion markers\n     */\n    public RecordFilter(final long currentTime, final long deleteRetentionMs) {\n        this.currentTime = currentTime;\n        this.deleteRetentionMs = deleteRetentionMs;\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Check whether the full batch can be discarded without inspecting individual records.\n     *\n     * <p><b>Optimization:</b> This method is called first and avoids iteration overhead for\n     * batches that can be entirely discarded (e.g., all records are too old).</p>\n     *\n     * @param batch The {@link RecordBatch} to evaluate\n     * @return A {@link BatchRetentionResult} indicating the decision\n     */\n    protected abstract BatchRetentionResult checkBatchRetention(RecordBatch batch);\n\n    /**\n     * Check whether a record should be retained in the log.\n     *\n     * <p><b>Invocation:</b> This method is called only for records in batches that were not\n     * entirely discarded by {@link #checkBatchRetention(RecordBatch)}.</p>\n     *\n     * <p><b>Example Logic:</b> A real implementation might check:\n     * <ul>\n     *   <li>Record key uniqueness (keep only the latest version)</li>\n     *   <li>Record age (discard records older than the log retention period)</li>\n     *   <li>Tombstone retention (keep tombstones for a grace period to ensure eventual consistency)</li>\n     * </ul>\n     * </p>\n     *\n     * @param recordBatch The {@link RecordBatch} containing the record\n     * @param record The {@link Record} to evaluate\n     * @return {@code true} if the record should be kept, {@code false} if it should be discarded\n     */\n    protected abstract boolean shouldRetainRecord(RecordBatch recordBatch, Record record);\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Example 7: Mutable Method Documentation\n\n### BEFORE:\n```java\n@Override\npublic void setMaxTimestamp(TimestampType timestampType, long maxTimestamp) {\n    long
